O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	You, most dear sons, I have completed this book for you which is the last of medical science together with its fulfillment, and I have made an end by its explanations and through its elucidations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I should complete this for you with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is forbidden in our region and is alien to all, so its knowledge has been lost and diminished, and nothing remains of it but small descriptions in books from ancient times that have been passed down by hand.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	From this has come error and vanity, and intentions have become closed off, and knowledge is far away.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	Or it seems to me that I should revive it along with the order of this treatise according to the way of exposition and explanation and abbreviation; and I will come together with the forms of cautery instruments, and other tools for the work, along with their arrangement, as required by necessity.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason that no good master of surgery is found in our time, the art of medicine has been neglected.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for one who undertakes this to surpass in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that they know the judgment of limbs, and their forms and connections and separations, and have knowledge of bones, nerves, arms, and their number, and movement, along with moving and resting veins, and where they emerge.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And so Hippocrates says that a name with the (right) name is powerful, and with work is small; especially in the art of medicine.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you in the introduction of this book that one who is not knowledgeable about the aforementioned things should beware lest they err and harm people; as I have often seen many of those who involve themselves with this science, yet abandon reason and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a mad surgeon cut into an abscess of scrofula on a woman's neck, and he cut the arteries of the neck; so much blood came out that the woman fell dead in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And I saw another surgeon treat a stone in an elderly man's bladder, and the stone was large; he carried away with it a part of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to treat him, and saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and knew well that if it were cut, he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another surgeon who treated the Duke of our land for a broken leg, and with the break there was an open wound; and the surgeons, full of ignorance, set the fracture on top of the wound with strong bandages, leaving no room for drainage, and left it like that for some time; they ordered him not to untie it; and he remained like this until his whole leg became swollen, his foot too, and came close to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to go to him, and I hurried to come and loosen his leg; and when I undid the bandages, he found peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But however the corruption was already confirmed in the member, and I could not heal it; and the corruption did not cease to spread through the member until the limb was completely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And then I saw another ulcer that burst and then inflamed due to the malignancy of its nature.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a cancer, when it is purified of melancholic humour, one should not touch it with an iron tool unless it is in such a place that everything corrupted can be entirely removed.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And therefore, dear son, you must know that manual work is divided into two categories: one where there is danger in multiple ways; and I will show you in each place of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	For this reason, it is necessary for you to be cautious, so that the foolish doctor cannot speak ill of you. Take up your weapons with prudence, approach your patients gently yet firmly, and employ the best method so that by God's grace you may bring them salvation and praise; leave aside those diseases which inspire horror due to their severity; cast off your weapons in places where they cause doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can journey from this world to the next with glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galen says in some of his admonitions: "Do not take up the treatment of any serious illness unless you are called a foolish doctor.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise in three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is about fire cauterization and medical treatment of acute diseases, and this chapter is arranged from the head down to the feet; it includes information on instrument forms, instruments for cauterization, and everything else necessary for the procedure.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and the use of cupping glasses and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar procedures; and this chapter is arranged with instructions on the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar issues; it is organized from the head to the feet, with instructions on the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Let us recall the work; it is necessary that I speak of the quality of aid and harm of each temperament.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of aid and harm is the longest speech and most subtle science and secret response; and many sages have spoken of this and agreed upon it; I will suffice with little of their words, for I fear length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cauterization aids universally in all constitutions where it is applicable, unless two constitutions: namely a warm constitution without matter and a dry constitution without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In the combination of warm and dry constitutions with matter, some argued that cauterization is greatly beneficial; while others said the opposite: that it has no value in illnesses caused by heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is so warm, and it should not be considered a treatment for warm illnesses caused by heat or dryness; and he who says otherwise argues that cauterization provides great relief to warm, dry illnesses occurring in men's bodies.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of man and its moisture to the constitution of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree to these words.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And in any case, let no one interfere except those who have experienced it, and who know by long practice the chapter on cauterization, and the diversity of human constitutions, and their dispositions and the causes of their illnesses, and their occurrences and the course of time; for other constitutions we have no fear, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the surgeons assembled and agreed on the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, my son, that fire cauterization is one of the secrets of healing, and of greater benefit than burning medical cautery.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and does not burn beyond the member which it heats, and harms no other part if properly used.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Caustic medicines spread from member to member in their operation, and give rise to diseases which are difficult to cure; and sometimes the fire kills the patient, not for its intensity nor for the goodness of its substance, but if there is any superfluity.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And this I have found through experiment and from long service and study in the art, and it is based on truth; And for that reason I excuse myself for being so lengthy, since I do not wish to take away your knowledge of the secret which lies within fire, and the quality of its work, how it cures diseases of bodies, as the philosopher says in demonstrating. Now receive this into your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, my son, they agreed on when the cauterizations should be performed and chose careful timing.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	I say that cauterization is suitable at any time, for the harmful effects are mitigated by its help; especially when cautery is required to ease pain and prevent further damage or complications in a limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think so, dear son, as some foolish surgeons do; for the illness that is healed by cautery has no relapse; and they say this thus: but it is not as they believe, because cauterization is a medicine which changes the complexion, dries out the humors causing pain, and is better than other medicines due to its swift action, its strength, and its effectiveness.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And it is a remarkable fact that the disease may come sometimes according to the complexion of the patient and the place where the disease is located as well as its virtue; superfluities are combined in him by the acquisition of food and similar things, unless cauterizations are administered at this place or where there is little superfluity and moisture, such as dental cauterization for pain, and similar things, and that kind of pain does not come back; but it happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cauterizations are called the last resort of medicine, and it is true; but they do not believe that cauterization follows after medicine, their intentions are false, and cauterization is indeed the last resort of medicine because when we administer various methods of treatment for a disease and they don't work, then we apply the cautery, and it succeeds.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore it is clear that cauterization is the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention of foolish physicians.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that cauterization with a golden instrument is better than with iron, and they claimed this was due to the quality of gold and its elevated nature; and they said that the site of cautery does not become infected, but this is not true as I have proven it myself, and found that in some people it does indeed get infected; and cauterization with gold is better than iron, just as they stated.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And yet when you heat a golden instrument, you do not know when it is hot by looking at the color of gold, and it cools down so quickly; and if one heats it too much, they damage their own eyes; thus there are enough reasons to refrain from using them.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this, we employ fire cauterization which we have adapted to our practice.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Here we have ordered this chapter from head to toe so that the information is easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	Olive oil cauterization.
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	These cauterizations are beneficial for moisture and cold affecting the brain, and there are two types done due to a disease called "soda", and because of excess humors descending from the head to the eyes, ears, causing numerous dreams, toothaches, sore throats, and especially all diseases arising from cold such as paralysis, apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The procedure for this cauterization is as follows: the patient is first purged with a solutive medicine that acts on the upper gastrointestinal tract, three or four nights according to their constitution and ability to tolerate it, then they are bled from the head.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then have him sit cross-legged between your hands, and place his hands on top of yours; after that, put the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two eyes; and leave it there until blood comes out, afterwards heat up the cautery called 'olivare', which is shaped like this:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	Place him on the spot marked with ink, and move your hand up and down while squeezing it repeatedly in a twisting motion; then lift your hand slightly, and check the spot if you see any bone there even just a little bit; if you don't see any, repeat the cauterization until you do as I told you; afterwards take a pouch of fine woolen fabric, put some soft cotton inside it, place it on the spot, and leave it for three days; after that apply softened butter-soaked cotton; keep it there until the burning sensation is gone; finally treat the wound with an ointment called 'tetrafarmacon' until it heals.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the ancients said, that the longer a wound remains open, the more it purges; and for this reason it heals quicker.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they said one must leave the cautery in place until a part of the bone is burnt, and then remove that which has been burnt from the bone, and it shall be healed.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And others say one must leave the cautery in place, pushing it as hard as you can until some bone is knocked out, just like the wide needles women use for their seams so that the humours come out faster; and one must let the wound remain open for a long time; afterwards, it shall be cleansed and sewn up.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cautery do not seem to me good at all in any way, except for some men where there is a chance of fear; and it seems to me that I should leave the head alone; because the head is weakened by continuous natural processes, as we show with other limbs; and even when the patient's head is naturally weak, and the first method of cautery appears more suitable and expedient to me, and so I use this in my work.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	From the old pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When in the entire head there is chronic pain that lasts a long time, the patient must use herbs and pills called 'cochie', as well as purgatives for the head, oils, and plasters; if one applies the cautery we mentioned earlier to them, and it does not help.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care if the patient's shoulder is of a strong nature and not too cold; in that case, cauterize beneath with a small cautery other than the one we mentioned above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	Afterwards, make a cautery on each corner of the head up to the bone, as we said before, and make one at the place called 'vasselz'; there are places where leeches are applied; lessen your hand's strength so that you do not go down to the bone: the patient will feel much more pain in this cautery than in others, and I shall speak of it later; and the cauteries on the corners must be gentler than those used for the middle part of the head, and here is how to do them:
dou cautere dou chief	For cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When sudden pain occurs in a part of the head and extends up to the eye, and the skull is cleansed by purifying medicines, and other treatments I have mentioned for dividing illnesses are performed, but none of these help: then you must make cauterizations according to two methods, that is, with medicine and with fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	Medicinal water cautery involves taking a fresh almond and removing its skin, cut it into two pieces, then make an incision in the temple where the pain resides in such a way that you can place the almond beneath the skin; when it is placed, bind and press it well, leaving it like this for twelve hours; afterwards, release the binding, apply pressure with the fresh almond, and leave the wound for two or three days; then apply cotton soaked in butter until it heals.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment, make sure it is healed; and if you wish to do so, apply some of the combusting medicinal substances that I have described in my twelfth treatise on combusting medications.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery is performed according to this method.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery, which has this shape.
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	It is called a 'clos' due to its head being shaped like a claw with a slight curve, and having a small appearance at the middle; place it on the painful area, and handle it so as to turn the iron slightly such that half of the heart-shaped edge is burned; lift your hand so as not to burn the artery which lies outside, and let the blood flow abundantly.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After put cotton in aw of flax, and place it over the spot for III days; then apply moist cotton in butter, and subsequently cleanse the area of ointment until it is healed; and if you wish to cauterize this migraine with the cautery called "cultellare," use all its pointed edge, and be cautious not to cut the artery during this operation on a fresh headache.
de emigraine	of migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat migraine as we mentioned before in the division of illnesses, and it does not improve, and you see that the cauteries previously described by medicine and iron do not suffice for him, then it is necessary that you heat the cautery called "cultellare" until it becomes white; and cauterize over the spot with a line half an inch long, and remove your hand once, ensuring you avoid cutting the artery and reaching the bone; and be careful of the mandible's movement when one chews, so that the jaw doesn't move nor spasms appear in the patient, and watch out for bleeding from the artery if it is cut, which has great risk especially for those unfamiliar with this procedure who are not students or experienced; and stop the work halfway. But I will tell you how to staunch blood when an artery is cut, and I shall show where it occurs in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that these cauterizations are not sufficient for the illness, and the patient is still suffering, cauterize him near the head as we have said before, and treat the wound until it heals; and if you wish, apply the cauterization method we mentioned in the chapter on arterial extraction, using the double-bladed cautery instrument; this type of cauterization is better and more effective than the previous one.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	From the pain in the ears due to cold.
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When there is pain in the ear due to cold, and one has applied solvent medicines and other treatments as we have mentioned before, but the pain persists, then heat this cauterization point called "poin", which takes the following form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After prick all around the sick ear, or both if the pain is in both ears, and move away a little above the root of the ear once you have marked the place to incise; and make ten pricks around each ear; then treat the area until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	For the torture of the mouth...
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Torture that must be treated with cauterization is only for those caused by moisture, as we have said in the division of diseases; and do not use cautery on similar cases arising from dryness and nerve spasms.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this similar case of torture caused by moisture from water and head washings, and gargling, and it does not improve, then you must cauterize the patient with three cauterizations: one at the root of the ear, another slightly outside the temple, and a third at the junction of the two lips; place the cautery on the part that appears healthy, and make the cautery towards the head of the ear a little below the horn of the head, and another in the temple as long as a thumb; leave the cautery until half of the heart's duration has passed; this is the shape of the cautery...
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it is similar to the surgical knife we mentioned earlier, but it is a little more delicate and requires a slightly thicker blade; treat the wound as I previously stated, until it heals.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is an old condition and you treat it as we have described, but there is no improvement, and the patient has no fever, then perform four cauterizations: two on the two corners of the head, one in the middle of the head, and one at the location called "vessel" as previously mentioned, and the last cautery on the mouth of the stomach; treat them as we have said before.
de litargie	Of lethargy.
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this illness, give the patient large herbs and pills to cleanse the brain; afterward, rub the entire head of the patient, and apply a mustard plaster on the occiput as written in the treatise on plasters; and here is how you perform the cautery: do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it is healed like this, it is good; and if not, apply three cauterizations to him from within the head down to the neck, with two finger-widths of space between each cautery; treat it as you would others, and if you see fit to do so, and the patient can tolerate it, apply one cautery in the middle; and if necessary, two more on the two corners, treating until it is healed; and let the cauterization be that which is called "olive oil," as I said before.
de la froidor dou chief	From the coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	The head must be cleaned of hairs and other things we have previously mentioned; then scrape the patient's head, followed by a cauterization in the middle of the head and on each corner, one behind, and three on the spine of the neck; if you need to do more, and the body is moist and the patient can tolerate it, and the illness is severe, apply four cauterizations on the spine of the back; let them remain until the greatest part of the heart is burned, then lift your hand away; treat until it is healed, and let the cauterization be that which is called "olive oil," as we have said before.
de l’epilempsie	Of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epileptic should not undergo fire cauterization unless they are phlegmatic, and it is necessary to first modify the brain with herbs and other treatments as we have mentioned in the section on treating severe patients who cannot tolerate medication.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is a child who cannot endure this, perform gargling and chewing while modifying the brain often with good meats; then raise their head in the middle, and perform the cauterization as we have mentioned before, and cauterize on the vessel and each corner; and if the patient is strong and can tolerate it, perform cauterizations as I said for one who has paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cauterizations be with olive oil as I have described.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, apply the subtle cautery as follows:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When the cause is due to melancholy, stemming from excess or corrupted moisture and thick phlegm, then apply cautery with thin irons as we have mentioned for those suffering paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if the cause is melancholy arising from excess descending into it, and the patient's body is moist, then give them something to drink so that their brain is cleansed, according to what was mentioned earlier in the classification.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that, bind the patient's head with a well-made linen cloth, like a cap, placing it in the middle of their head; have them sit cross-legged and be securely held on all sides; then apply the liniment, using old sheep butter instead; heat it over a gentle fire so that its warmth can be tolerated by the skin when applied; then empty out the cap from within the head, let it cool down; perform this procedure once weekly with another good treatment until they are healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	And if you wish to cauterize with points, make many points throughout the entire cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This manner of cautery softens the brain greatly; then apply moist cotton soaked in butter and goose fat.
de l’awe des eulz	of the eyes' awe
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When awe first comes to the eyes through the signs I have mentioned in the section above, then begin and give the patient something cleansing for the head, protect it from all moisture, and make them sweat in a bath many times while fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After, instruct them to cover their head, and perform a cautery between the temples, performing two cauteries if the descent of awe is to both eyes together or one if it is only to one; take care to avoid all veins and arteries beneath the heart, and let the cauteries be long according to the width of the temple; guard against excessive blood loss, and should you see too much blood escape, staunch it with such power as you are able.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And I will instruct you in the extraction of arteries and the incision, being cautious of how to staunch it; sometimes cauterization is performed beneath the two hind bones.
dou cors des larmes	The body of tears.
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	When tears from the eyes are ancient and accustomed to flow along the veins, or near the arteries which appear outside the head; and one can see that these are cold phlegmatic superfluities, then one should perform the cauterization as I mentioned at the beginning on the eye: I cautery in the middle of the head, II cauteries over the two temples, and II cauteries beneath the two hind bones; and if more is needed, carefully cauterize above the eyebrow with several small cauteries.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	From the body of tears through the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you treat him according to what we have said in the division, and he does not benefit from it, then give the patient to drink three nights with cock's meat; after, raise his head, and cauterize him in the middle of the olive-shaped part; make two 'clavilis' cauteries on the two wrists, a little below the hairline; be cautious of the artery so as not to cut it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the 'clavilis' cautery:
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the pupil of the eye is softened by illness and moisture, then cauterize it with this cautery which is called 'olivare'.
de coi ci est li forme:	from which this takes shape:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see fit to make two cauterizations on the two joints as long as the hair is; and do not remove your hand until a third of the paper has burned, according to the manner I have described.
dou poil qui point l’oil	of the hair which pricks the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	At times it happens that the hairs of the eyes turn inward and prick the eye, requiring cauterization according to two methods; that is, with fire or burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they are born and are equal in length, then place the patient on your bench; afterwards mark above the paper of the eyes a figure that is similar to the leaf of myrtle, and let the beginning of the sign be near the hairs; then apply cotton moistened with egg white and parsley poultice onto the eye, then heat up the following cautery:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterizing on the marked figure several times until the heart of the sore is burnt out; and the sign of a successful operation is that you see the paper withdrawing, and the hairs rising at the tip of the eye; then remove your hand, and leave it like this for three days, then apply cotton moistened with butter until the scald is gone; afterwards treat with ointment until healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if after this the hairs grow back and the skin is softened again, then resume the cautery on that same spot as you did initially; but if the hairs are gone, cauterize it until the skin rises to its natural level, making sure it's even and doesn't prick the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The burning cauterization of medicine is when you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow large and even, then make a parchment in the shape of a myrtle leaf; take French soap and live coal, each weighing 3 ounces, and grind them together well; do this quickly so it doesn't cool, then spread it onto the mold you made like the myrtle leaf, placing it on the skin around the eyes; if the patient's ailment is only in one eye, operate on that one, but if both are affected as well; place under the eye cotton moistened with egg white; keep the patient's head steady and place your own finger over the medicine, pressing gently with two fingers every time the patient feels a stinging sensation from the medicine, for it will sting like fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, remove the medicine with your hand.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the coagulation has passed, lift the edge of the wound, and observe if you see the flesh raised as it was lifted by the cautery or incision; and if it is so, then it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If not, apply more medicine to the place where it has not worked, until your work is even, and your eyes are precise; then put moist cotton wool on butter until the burning feeling subsides, afterward treat the wound with an ointment called 'dyafenis' or another, until it heals.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you need to, be careful in your work with great vigilance so that the medicine does not touch the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the paper becomes soft afterward, and the hairs prick in the eye, then restart the medicine on that softened area with the paper specifically, just as you did before; after curing it until it is healed; and this is the shape of the myrtle leaf:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of men are diverse in size and smallness, and according to this, let your treatments be determined; and do not neglect the correct path for one who studies this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	on the treatment of fistula by cauterization
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your treatments do not benefit it, then you must perform cauterization in this way.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	For the sick person, command that he place his head on your palm; hold his head firmly between your hands so it does not move or slip away from you; then apply moist cotton wool soaked in egg white or parsley juice to the eye; afterwards heat up the following cautery tool: a quill-shaped piece with a pointed end like a feather, and also a tent shape at one end, although both are suitable for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	Then press the fistula if it is open and remove any pus, then dry it; if it is closed, operate on it and draw out whatever matter there may be inside the bowels; afterwards apply a hot cautery in this form, and hold your hand over the cautery at the knuckle above the eye so that your hands do not move around excessively; place the cautery on the eyelid's fatty tissue and burn it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you reach the bone with the cautery at the beginning, it would be beneficial.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, restart the cautery again and repeat if needed, leaving it for three days. Afterwards, apply moist cotton soaked in butter, and treat with a drying ointment until it is healed. If forty days pass without healing, use corrosive medicine to expose the bone; and proceed according to what is outlined in this chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	There is also a method of cauterizing a fistula, which none of the ancients mentioned.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	In the case of a fistula, pierce its location, then insert into the opening one fine camel-hair, which matches its shape.
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	et they make it to the quantity of one third of a pound; and hold your hand or arm firmly, and do not let the patient move at all, so that the molten lead does not flow into his eye; and be sure you place on the patient's eye moist cotton in egg white or milk: the lead will quickly close the fistula, and the wound will heal with wonderful health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cauterization we have mentioned, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, you must administer the perforation to the nail, and restore the fistula to the body of the nail according to what is necessary in its proper place.
des crevaices en levres	Cracks in lips.
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Often occur cracks in lips called "hairs," especially in children's lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks as described in the previous sections, and the treatment is ineffective, then heat a small knife-shaped cautery according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	Place it on the cracks with pressure until it reaches the bottom; afterward, treat the area with wax until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	on abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess forms at the root of the throat or in the uvula, palate, or tooth roots, it causes decay and becomes enlarged, festering, and turns into a fistula; you treat it as described previously, but if it doesn't heal: then take a cautery according to the size of the fistula; next, dilate the opening of the fistula, and hold your hand so that the hot iron reaches the bottom and back of it; do this once or twice, afterward treating it as described in wound treatment, until it is healed; if it heals thus, it's good; if not, then you must uncover the area and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you find in its respective chapter.
dou movement des dens	Through the movement of teeth.
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicine but it is not effective, then place the patient's head on your lap; afterward, heat the cautery which will be formed as follows: put a stick over the tooth; insert the hot cautery into it until the patient feels the heat reaching the root of the tooth; then remove your hand and repeat the cautery according to your desire; afterwards, have the patient fill their mouth with salty water, and keep it there for an hour, rinsing frequently.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	In this way, the moving tooth becomes confirmed in its place, and the softened gum is restrained, while any corrupt moisture dries up.
de la dolor des dens	From toothache
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When toothache comes from the cold, or there is a chill in the air and medicines do not help, then it requires cauterization done in two ways: butter cautery and fire cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Butter cautery is done like this: take butter from a cow and place it in an iron or bronze spoon; afterward, take cotton and wrap it around the point of a needle, then moisten the cotton with boiling butter, placing it on the aching tooth for as long as necessary until it cools down. Do this frequently so that its healing properties can reach the root of the tooth. You may also dip wool and cotton in cold butter and place them on the painful tooth; put an iron rod to heat over fire until the flame reaches the tip of the needle, which will be placed on top of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	The cauterizations done with fire are such that you take a cane of iron or copper, and it should be thick so that the fire does not reach the patient's mouth; afterwards heat up the cauterization tool, from which its shape will come afterward, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand there until the cauterization is cooled down; do this often, for the pain shall be removed that very day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And the patient should fill their mouth with good butter during the urgency of this cauterization, and then let it cool down afterwards; and this is the shape of the cauterization tool:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make the cauterization of whichever cheek you want to, and according to your ability; and this is the shape of the cane:
des scrophules	Of scrofula.
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When scrofula is caused by phlegm and cold moisture, and it does not respond to digestion through medication, then heat the cautery with a chimney from which smoke emerges, and make two openings for the smoke to escape from the other side of the cautery; place the hot cautery on the abscess once or as needed until you reach its base; if the abscess is small, apply a cautery according to its size, and leave it there for three days; then apply moist cotton with butter until the burning sensation subsides; afterward, treat the area with ointments and bandages until it heals.
Li forme de la cainne:	The shape of the cane:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When moisture overcomes the channels of the lung, especially when it arises from cold constitution, then the patient should be first emptied by means of dissolving medicines; afterwards cauterize at the root of the throat, and take care not to reach the throat, but burn just a little above the heart.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterwards apply another cauterization at the junction of the neck and skull along the spinal column, let it be a "clavicle" type as described earlier in this document; treat the area as mentioned above until it is healed.
de la toust	Of the cough.
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When any lung disease is caused by cold moisture, and the patient lacks fever or dryness, especially if it is an old illness, then apply two cauterizations over the clavicle in sight; another cauterization between the breasts at the sternum; let these be "clavicle" type according to what was previously mentioned.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see fit, perform the fire cautery by pricking with a 'point', as previously described for ear ailments; and let there be thirty or so points, or slightly fewer.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After treating the site as previously stated, apply three-row cauteries in this manner:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And for these cauteries to be lighter, do three at a time.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	Of the shoulder dislocation:
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and cauterize the heart until it pierces right through to the ribs, and this would make up the shape of four cauterizations; and for this reason cautery is performed with a cauterizer that has three blades, therefore the figure of cauterization consists of six cauterizers; and these are the nerves according to their delicacy and this is the form of the cauterizer which has three blades:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	and at times it is adjusted on this one nerve so there are eight cauterizers.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	Afterwards apply the cauterizer and crush the blisters with salt; then let the patient rest, and do not move the limb for a long time until it is well-supported.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated again soon after, then immediately perform a cauterization on the thick part of the collarbone, or many cauterizations at once with intensity.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joints are closed, and moisture is removed, and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When cold and excessive moisture arise in the stomach to such an extent that they remove it from its normal state, and catarrh is multiplied within him, and with usual treatments he does not improve, then it is necessary that the patient be placed on their back, and extend their legs and hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	After that, make three cauterizations with a spoon-shaped instrument below the heel for the size of a thumb, let each cautery be fixed, and two cauteries outside both sides so that the shape of the cauterizations is triangular, and there should be enough space between them such that they do not join together when suppurating; and may the cauterization be so thorough as to purify both parts of the heart, and may the figure of the cauterizations follow this form without adjustment:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you want to cauterize with a large cautery in the stomach according to this method; and for those who fear this cautery, cauterize by pricking and bleeding on the stomach at one point according to the amount you wish to add; then cauterize with the entire cautery which is called "point".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the previous condition, once it is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	When the liver experiences pain due to cold and moisture and excessive gas, as it has become displaced from its natural state by superfluities; and the patient is treated as we have said in divisions, but it does not help them, then the patient must be reminded of their condition; apply three cauteries according to this form and figure and quantity on the liver, outside the hypochondria, where the flank of a man lies; leave a space between each cautery equal to the width of a finger; let the cauteries be as long as the body, and do not press too hard with your hand during the entire cautery process; only burn half the depth of the heart, and have the patient stand upright on their feet; if they cannot, then let them lie down, extend their legs, and lift their arms; this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And if your wish is to cauterize these cutellary cauteries, being skilled and wise in the art, be careful not to burn through the entire heart (muscle), for it would desiccate all of the body; nor that it reach the mouth (of the wound), since the heart is very delicate there, and you know this well.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When there is an abscess on the liver, and you wish to know if it lies within the flesh or membrane of the liver: if it's in the flesh, the patient experiences pain that is not too intense; however, if it's in the membrane, they feel excruciating pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And so when this wound should be examined, it is necessary that the patient is reminded of their condition on top of their head; then bleed heavily from the site where the abscess is located, and subsequently heat a cautery resembling a thorn for which this (form) is made.
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	Et cauterize the fire cautery until the heart is burnt, and it reaches the bone marrow, so that all cartilage is destroyed; after the cure, treat it according to the treatment of wounds until it is healed; and no one should use this cautery other than those who have studied medicine for a long time, by whose hands these illnesses have sometimes been cured.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then one may operate boldly, yet it seems to me that leaving [the wound] be is better.
dou cautere de pleuresin	The cautery of soft wax
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients say that one must make soft wax cauteries from the roots of aristolochia, and in this way: take a long root of aristolochia, the largest you can find, and let it be dry, also as thick and as long as your finger; dip it in oil, then take it to the fire, and cauterize with one cautery between the throat and neck, and two small cauteries just below on the part that is under the beard; two more cauteries between the fifth rib and sixth rib, sloping slightly behind; one cautery at the navel, another above the stomach, and one between the two shoulders, plus two on either side of the navel external to the cautery between the shoulders; do not press your hand too hard, but rather be gentle like when perfuming.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And some ancients said that any man should use a fire cautery like a razor, heating it and placing it between the ribs until it reaches the abscess; if it burns away the pain, just as we have said for an abscess of the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work, there is fear that the patient may die now, or a fistula may form which cannot be healed.
de la mice	From the mouse.
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the mouse as we have said in the sections on treatments, and it does not improve, then there are three types of cautery which are all good.
