From the incision that is below the temple up to the second incision; scrape out all the core that is between the two slits down to the bone, then do the same from the middle incision to the other second one, and then remove this spatomile.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	Insert into the first slit the instrument which is called a 'cultellarium', and it is very sharp on one side, but soft and not sharp on the other side, and this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	Place the sharp edge towards the flesh near the core and the soft edge towards the bone, and insert it until it reaches the middle slit.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And scrape out all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes as long as the incision is continuous up until it reaches the core; then do the same in the middle slit down to the other exterior one; and then drain the blood evenly, and express the place for the blood clotting; then insert in each slit a tent made of old cotton, and apply wet swabs soaked in wine, oil, and eggs, and ensure that no hot abscess forms there; on the third day remove the bandage and irrigate it with a great application of warm water, then treat it with basilicon ointment mixed with rosehip oil, as well as other treatments used for wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	Of eye rheum.
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When to someone comes acute accustomed catarrh, and you see the eyes sunken and small, and weakened sight, and burned sclera; and the hair falls out, and in the head an aching pain, and the patient sneezes; then know by these symptoms that these discharges and this catarrh come from many veins, and to heal it use this method.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And you should instruct the patient to lie on their back, then make a big incision in the middle of the forehead, and another from ear to ear.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	Beginning from the incision of the left temple towards the right one, let it be cut up to the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move with eating; and when the bone is exposed, wipe all the blood with a sponge, and then sew between the two lips of the incision an old cotton pad, and linum bandages; then bind above moistened cloths in wine and oil, and be aware of hot abscesses; once it is removed, you must rub the bone until flesh begins to grow there, then treat it with drying substances that promote healing.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this way: take two parts wheat flower and four parts colophony to make a plaster; administer it on these wounds in order to generate flesh all over.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Cleaning of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Anything that falls into the ears is one of four things: grains, insects, rocks or similar metals; seeds such as nuts, beans, peas; or flowing substances like water and oils and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When a stone or any other object that does not fit the ear falls into it, and cannot grow in the ear, place the ear under sunlight.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, drip a few drops of violet oil or sesame oil and administer an extraction; have them sneeze often, then block their nostrils when sneezing comes on, and place pieces of fine cloth or wool around the ear; keep the ear elevated.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Often fire comes forth through this cure; and if it does not come forth, one must apply extraction with subtle pincers, of which the form is thus:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it fires with the pincers, it is good; if not, apply extraction with a subtle curved hook of small size; and if it does not fire with this, make a pipe of copper and push the head of the pipe into the ear canal forcefully, stopping up what is around the pipe with soft wax so that air cannot enter along with the pipe; then pull strongly on the ear, for often it fires as we have said; and if it does not fire in such a manner, take birdlime and put some instrument with a point onto it, wrap a bit of cotton around this, then press the birdlime onto the stone or whatever it is, and draw out the fire.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she cannot be cured of all these things that we have said, then hasten to split the ear rather than let a hot abscess come, and spasm; and the way of the incision is such that you first bleed the patient with a cephalic vein cut, and extract blood according to its measure and virtue, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn their ear upwards, and make a small incision in the root of the ear at the fat where it depends; and let the incision be like a crescent moon, so that you reach the stone, then remove it as best you can, and suck it quickly to your mouth; and treat it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a grain that has formed and it swells, then administer an extraction; and if it cannot exit, then apply a very thin spatula in this way...
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	And bring about an incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think the grain is moist due to ear moisture, until you have made many incisions; then extract it with subtle pincers and sucking, as we have said, so that the extraction is eased.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the case of water that falls into the ear, the patient should first sneeze and fill the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let them lie on that same ear where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it should jump out because of this, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If not, take many pebbles according to the length of your thumb, thin and light, and warm them slightly over fire; place them in the patient's ear opening, and jump on it with their feet from another side, pressing down on the stone that is in the ear with another pebble; do not stop doing this, stone by stone until all the water drains out, and thus let it drain entirely; if you wish, take a single reed, insert one end into the ear, and light the other end on fire until most of the reed has burned away; then repeat again with other reeds until all the water is drained as we have said for stones.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the beast, if it is small like a flea or similar, treat it as we have mentioned in the division; but if it is large and can be felt, use tweezers for extraction; this is the lightest thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	When extracting worms embedded in the ears, if you treat it as we have said in the division and use remedies for distillation but the treatment is ineffective, then examine the ear in sunlight; if any worms are visible, remove them with fine tweezers, and if none appear, use a small stick to search.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it is narrow beneath and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	Insert the finest point into the ear according to the extent of the patient's suffering, then suck strongly with the entire stick; do this often until all the worms emerge.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not obey and come out, plug the canal with cotton as I have said for stones; and if they do not exit as we have mentioned, administer distillations that the ancients have tested in worm occlusions, and you will find them in the treatise on distillations; and so distil your oils and medicines into the ear for all these instruments, this is how it looks:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	Let it be made of silver or copper, narrow below at the small openings, and wide above for distillation; and to press within the distillation into the instrument of well-made brass for this purpose, and if you wish take a shaver and wrap around its point appropriately with cotton; then pour your oil or juice, and what you wish of your medicines into the canal, and let the canal be in the ear; then put within the shaver all the cotton, and press your hand steadily so that the oil is distilled to the end of the ear; and the patient will feel it inside, and let the distillation pot be heated over the fire until you distil it into the ear; and take care that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be as effective.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stuffing of ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without holes in their ears; and the same happens to men due to blockage from a wound or growth inside the ear, and this blockage sometimes becomes embedded in the ear, so it cannot be seen; and sometimes the hole appears outside the ear, and can be well observed.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which is embedded and cannot be seen requires prompt treatment in many cases, and for this visible one, you must place the ear of the patient towards the sun; look inside: if you see any opaque appearance, treat with all these medicines which follow.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And it should be sharp and pointed at the front and back, but not harming the ear; if the opaque appearance is from a growth or flesh of the ear, take subtle pincers, and gently remove all this flesh.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the suppurations are complete in the ear, take a delicate, lightweight razor and warm it slightly over fire, then place it on the body of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you detect suppuration that causes itching for the patient when they hear sounds, pierce lightly and be mindful not to damage the ear nerves; then insert into the ear a tent according to the width of the hole, and soak it in Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this every day until the wound is healed, take a tent and dip it in rosewater, then sprinkle crushed vitriol on top; if you see swelling in the ear, remove the tent and insert another one soaked in cerate made from almond oil and wax, until the swelling subsides; then treat it until it's completely healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if there is loss of blood, immerse a sponge and cloth in cold water, place it on the ear, and employ other remedies that stop the flow of blood as described in the chapter on distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the paper flesh
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	These eye ailments that come about due to moist and dry papers, you should treat with tongs and forceps, scraping the root bark of a spindle tree; then apply crushed green vitriol to the site.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if there is no discharge, then apply a subtle lenticular cautery; the cauterizer should be applied after the incision and moved around; often repeated until nothing remains of its root; for when they are cauterized with fire, those roots are burned away and do not return.
de la gresle	of the hail
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times on paper there are things that appear like hail in form and hardness, and for this reason, this illness is called "grandine," which is an assembly of thick moisture on the paper above and below; the work is such: take care if the grandine moves from one part to another, and it is a minor thing to know; thus cut it widely, then peel each side lightly, then take pincers and remove it.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	if you cannot remove it without piercing the paper slightly, it does not harm the patient; and if the tear is large, join it with a suture, treating it until it is healed; and if it is small, make no effort, for ointments will restore it quickly and promote flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the hailstone is descending into the ear towards the upper part, it turns the membrane inside out, and grasp the hailstone with some pincers, and cut and press it from one side to another; and if the membrane is removed by incision, this does not cause harm; and when the hailstone is extracted, so wash the eye with salty water, and treat the place where unhealthy flesh grows until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	from the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Echinach is a fat that forms in the eye membranes above, and this happens more often to children than adults, and it greatly harms their eyes, causing them cataracts in the mornings, and they cannot bear to look at the sunlight because tears rush to their eyes; because of this, they lie down on their faces headfirst, and sleep like that, with their eye membranes beneath their eyebrows moistened by the echinach which appears in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press down on the place with your fingers and feel the exit point between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	The method of the operation is as follows: have the patient place their head on your lap; then take a linen cloth and prepare a cone-shaped cover according to the amount that will be removed from each part, then place it on them; press with your fingers from one side to the other so that the exit point is within the circle; then make an incision in the middle of the moisture using a sharp spatula, but not larger than the wound made when opening a vein; and cut through the skin thoroughly until you reach the exit point; often, the substance will come out of the incision resembling a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Pull it out then with one piece of cloth padding between your two fingers on top, and turn your hand right and left so that the spatulum is evenly spread; be careful not to insert into the crack, or you may injure the eye.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	If the spatulum does not emerge at first from the crack, slightly increase the size of the opening until it appears; then extract it as we have described, then wet pads with vinegar and water, place them on the site, and apply bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	For such people who grind herbs and place them on to corrupt the moisture that has remained.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it until it is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to a hot abscess, treat it with soothing emollient plasters until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	hairs of paper.
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow on paper that are not natural and are inflamed, they harm the eyes, causing various diseases such as habitual tears and softening of the papers and albuginea, leading to eye destruction; it is treated in four ways: with cautery by fire, or medicine according to what was said before in the chapter on cautery, and done either by incision and suturing or by canes, depending on what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	Place the patient's head in your lap, then turn the paper of the eye towards your left hand; if it is inverted, that is good; otherwise, insert a needle with all its thread above it; and whether this be near the margin of the paper where the hairs grow close to these hairs, draw the thread over all the paper, and turn it on a razor; then make an incision in the part beneath the paper, under the appended hairs, for the full length cutting away the entire thickness from the large tear duct down to the small one; next remove the thread, and place below the paper a little tent of cotton and linen, then sign upon the paper a figure of ivy, but be sure that the figure is proportioned to the extent to which you wish to raise the divided paper.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	Et si a teil qui a mestier c'on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; 
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then cut this which overcomes the small forces equally according to the form which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the forceps, and the thing is not equal, take a needle with thread in it, place one end of the thread on your face; pass the other thread through the large tear, and the second thread through the small one, then gather the two threads evenly between your fingers; lift your hand equally, and raise all the skin you have gripped as we have explained earlier, then join the two lips of the wound by stitching, and cure it until it is healed; if an abscess forms around the incision, treat it with a cauterization using cerate ointment or similar soothing remedies; sometimes the hair on the membrane becomes inverted: in such cases you must follow the instructions we have given for incisions; but the sutures in both instances are more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of ulcers is done in this way: you must fold the paper and make a slit inside according to what I have said; then you make two canes per wound, two fine cords as long as the width of your thumb, and cut at both ends where you hold the threads together. Then join one part with the other carefully over that which stands above in the eye of the paper, and stretch the two canes from their respective ends: leave it thus for a few days until the skin stretches and becomes black and putrid, so much so that it falls by itself
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it takes a long time to cure, cut the ulcer with forceps and treat it until it is healed. Once the wound has closed up completely and you can lift off the paper without hurting the patient too much, remove any hairs that have started growing again; these are the two kinds of canes that you will make according to this shape and in this quantity: length-wise and width-wise
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	li ovraiges est telz that you take a fine needle and thread it with soft, fine silk; then join the heads and tie one end to the other carefully, making sure the length of thread is about as long as a palm's width; next attach another fine silk thread briefly in the eye of the needle; knot both ends together; have your patient place his head on top of yours so that sunlight falls directly onto the work at hand because this type job requires delicacy and precision; insert your needle through all parts toward base near hair root quickly enough without damaging natural hairs but deep enough beneath skin surface until you reach paper underneath; remove natural hairs one by one from hole created earlier then put them back inside same place they came out from originally along with any additional ones removed during procedure (one or two, three more perhaps); finally withdraw hand gently so as not damage natural hair growth direction pulling all newly inserted strands towards papery surface alongside original shaft.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the arrow is treated and the hair does not come out with it, you will treat the arrow from below along all the thread that you have arranged for it, until the arrow comes out of the hole above and you see it by the vision of the eye; then you will remove the arrow and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed II or III days, until the hair withers in its place and flesh grows over it; and if the hair is small, accompany one long natural hair from the head hairs, and raise it up with that (hair) which you leave, until it lengthens and then remove it.
de la porriture de l’oil	From the corruption of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this illness called "aleacrati" or the corruption comes into the eye, there are two types of it: one natural and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And this occurs suddenly due to a wound, or from a cutting instrument or cauterization, and through similar procedures.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the method of treatment involves cutting through that scar and separating its lips, then placing linen cloths inside and binding it until it is healed; one must not use things that dry out or constrict in treating this injury.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do not, the illness will return worse than before; but use softening substances instead, such as fenugreek; and boil flax seeds in water or some other liquid along with linseed oil, melted diaqilon grease in any kind of oil, wrap a cloth around it, and treat him like that.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the secret to your treatment is that you must ensure it does not heal according to its previous form; and these procedures we have mentioned are only initial measures against this illness so that it may never return in its former state.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	from flesh which comes to the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease, which is dislocated and truly called "axacrati", is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wounds and cuts and cauterization and similar things; and the way of operating on it is to take a needle with double thread, insert it into the flesh, make it pierce from left eyelid up to right, so that the threads come out in two places of the flesh; then stretch the flesh above the entire needle and cut with a spatula one finger wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure on the paper returns as it should, that's good; if not, take a razor and place it in the incision, turn the paper over, and make two cuts along its edges inside the paper; let the ends of these two incisions be at the angles of the cut you made, and make the angles so that when they are put together, the figure is like that of a letter with the name "Greek"; then remove this flesh, according to how much its sides reach underneath the paper, from what follows the paper, then join the two parted parts, and sew them with a thread of wool; then treat it as we have said regarding softening medicines and bandages until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the illness comes from a tear or a suture or cauterization, you must make an incision filled with paper beneath the hairs and according to what was previously mentioned; then sever between the two flaps of skin like I said before; one should do work based on the form of the disease, since it is very diverse in its forms, and wise masters use all their power to fashion an appliance that will restore figure to its natural form; and even the sick themselves, according to what is required for them in terms of work and instruments in various arrangements.
dou soudement de la papiere	Suddenly from paper...
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suturing occurs on the hands of men in such a way that the paper above is adhered with eye-white, and it cannot move nor perform its natural works, you must therefore insert the tip of a razor beneath the paper and lift it up; extend it to pincers so that you cut what is hardened by a subtle spatula, which should not be too sharp or too blunt, such that the patient may not suffer if the spatula is too sharp and pierce the eye; let your incision, from which you peel away this assembly, be lightly made, such that the paper returns to its natural form; and heal all of this assembly with a salty eyewash, then rinse it with warm water, and collarbone oil; then place between the paper and the eye a tent of linen, and put on top of the eye wool moistened in egg white; after three days use of the collarbone oil and sealing things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	Of the nail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the nail is according to two manners: it is nervous and similar to hard sinew, and another which is not nervous, but is like white frozen moisture, when touched by iron and one thinks to remove it with pincers, it cannot be done; both appearances begin towards the great tear duct, and grow little by little until they cover all sight, light, and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is as follows: let the patient put their head towards your hand, then open their eyes; lift up the eyelid with your hand, then coil the nail with small tweezers and extend it upward; then take a needle, and place within it a horsehair, or cow hair, or ox hair, and strong thread; double the point of the needle slightly and insert it into the nail, piercing through completely with the needle, and tie the nail with one thread and extend it upwards, then scrape away all the hair on the side of the nail which is attached to the eyeball and the eyelid up until the head, then cut off the remainder at the root of the tear duct with a very sharp spatula and small forceps, and leave the natural flesh around the tear duct so that through incision, the body of tears may flow as usual; sometimes you extend the nail only towards the eyelids, and to one thread, just as we have said; then scrape it off completely with a spatula made thus:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And make sure the spatula does not touch the fleshy membrane and tear it, and that the plumule is not pierced; after incising pour some crushed silphium into the eye, and a collar made of litharge, and leave this until the next day; then treat with what is necessary until it heals.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nervous and you cannot insert the needle, and the uncines cannot enter it, this similar condition of a nail has often been treated by physicians; they grow as I have described in the division, and if you see them cut off, treat the patient's eye, and take a light spatula with a small sharp point according to this shape:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And lift the nail carefully from above, and if you see that it does not decrease in size and the root presses against it, then drip from your mouth into the eye a distillate of litharge and red lead collar, and silphium powder; pack the eye until the next day; then repeat this operation according to these same actions until it is entirely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing opposes you in the eye, such as a hot abscess, then milk it, and treat first the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of flesh around the tear duct causes great harm to the eye, suspend it with a hook, and cut off a part but not all, so that body fluids do not flow out; then instil in the eye red colloy made from litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows on the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	In the eyes of some men, red flesh sometimes grows, covering the pupil and spreading onto the cornea, resembling a rose with its petals; the procedure is that the patient rests his head on your lap, then you open their eyes, and coil all this flesh around hooks suitable for it, holding it tightly; then cut off the first bit of flesh, and go on cutting with a razor until the end, taking care not to injure the eye while working; and let the incision be made by a small knife like we said in the chapter about nail incisions and small forces that one removes the nail with, as the form after this chapter shows; and once the incision is complete and all flesh removed, fill the eye with pounded wax or instil red colloy and similar corrosive medicines, and put cotton mixed with egg white over the eye so it is protected from a hot abscess; if anything remains, and your blood boils due to heat, and you suspect a hot abscess, leave the eye alone and treat the abscess with things that calm down hot abscesses; then return to your work until it is healed, and thus do whenever flesh grows in the eye like this.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nevertheless, you must ease the treatment of each weak eye through natural means; and through accidental intervention using iron tools; never thrust your hand into any of these procedures until you see that this limb can withstand the procedure.
des voines des eulz	the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Below the veins are red lines that cover the eye, obscuring its sight and weakening it daily.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary for the first step to examine the eye and see where it is red, ensuring that there are no other ailments besides redness; then twist it in such a way: instruct the patient to place their head on your lap, then stretch those veins as much as possible according to your knowledge, being careful with delicate ones twice over in this manner.
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	Et let there be two ounces by degrees in the body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	then you must gently coil the forces of these veins, and wipe away the blood hour after another, until you see the removal of those veins from the eye; and be careful not to injure the eye with the points of spatulas, and perform this work at noon in front of the sun, being very fervent in your task so that you only cut those veins; and when you have done this, then distill green and red collyrium into the eye to corrupt what remains from the sebaceous gland.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are not able to collect all of it in that hour, then make a plaster over the eye with things that soothe the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain is soothed and the abscess is warm, then begin again according to this method which is before, until it is healed; and this is the form of the forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	Of the eye's fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The surgeon calls it an "arissati" fistula: when you treat it with cauterization and burning medicine as I have previously mentioned, and it is not healed, there is pus within that you must cut open over the abscess, where it should die, and drain all the moisture until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and blackness, take all the instrument of which this has the shape; and it is called an "aspre chief", and make it of iron until the head returns, and point it like a file as it is in its present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place it on the place of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two fingers, and press your hand a little so that you know this corruption is removed; do this once or twice, then restore the place with drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	if the wound is healed and flesh has grown in it, and the body of the fistula is closed, and remains so for forty days, and does not reopen or become abscessed again, and no bad accident occurs there, know that it is cured; if this is not the case, then there is another means to restore the fistula at the site of its origin according to this method: you should expose the bone a second time with an iron tool and sharp medicine; when it has been exposed, take one rod made like this, which must have three angles, and let the piece be tapered down towards the end as shown here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	place it over the bone near the elbow, and withdraw your hand one palm's length from the eye, then turn the drill completely until it pierces the bone so that the patient feels the wind go through it when he holds his hand above his knuckles; you may restore the site with dry medicines as I have taught you, and once the flesh forms and hardens over the hole, the matter will descend into the fistula, which is a more gentle process for the sick person.
de l’issue de l’oil	From the exit of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye opens completely without any obstruction or impairment of the nerve, you must bind the patient; then treat it and apply cupping glasses or leeches without injury to suck out the blood, then place on the eye a poultice made from aconite, aloes, incense, and gum; then extract the eye and place the plaster on bandages and soft cloths. The method of the cloths is such that you take very soft cloths and fold each one into four layers, then place one upon another according to the quantity required by the eye. Then bind it firmly with a stiff bandage, and reapply cupping glasses to suck out blood without injury; then remove the glasses and leave the eye extracted day and night, and if the poultice softens you must tightly extract it again; then remove the binding after the day and night have passed, and if you see that the eye is healing it's good; but if not, reapply the plaster, cloths, bindings, and cupping glasses until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	From the rupture of a hard membrane
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruption occurs in the hard membrane, it breaks open and expels a material like resin grains, which is awful to see; if you decide to operate on it, the procedure involves inserting a needle into the root of one part underneath until reaching the upper part, then insert another needle with double thread from the eyelid area; pierce through, leaving the first needle in place according to its position; cut the double thread and tie a piece of membrane around it, securing it tightly, then extract the needle and apply moist wool soaked in egg on the eye; leave until the threads dry along with the membrane, then treat the eye with comforting substances until the wound is healed; sometimes the wound is constrained by membrane on each side with a circle of cloth until healing occurs.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye shows great bulging, pierce it with a subtle spatule that comes in perfect alignment with the eye, and drain out the white moisture and lower the eye, and enter (it) immediately; then extract it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the eye's bowels
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease which is called "alcunnati" affects only the bowels of the eye, appearing like descending water, but it is not water; and the way to treat this condition is for you to have the patient sit on a furnished seat that is upright, then take hold of their head with both hands, and move it until you see the bowels come above your eyes; then they will be cured, and the light will not descend nor become cloudy again, and the patient will be able to see things as they used to; but if the descent of water does not stop, know that it is indeed water, and if the descent of the bowels is not aligned as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	sit the patient between your hands, then take the fine spatula and make an incision on the horny membrane at one point along the continuation of the conjunctiva with the horny membrane and the cornea until the bowels are exposed; and when they have been removed, pour into the eye warm water mixed with honey, or water in which fenugreek has been boiled and honey, then treat it with another cure until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	Watery eyes
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have seen similar watery conditions in the eye, and what needs to be pierced for treatment; so we treat it according to health principles.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	Have the patient sit with crossed hands, facing away from the light to avoid sunlight, and tie the healthy eye shut very tightly; then place the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eyes are left, or right hand if they are right; then take in your right hand, if the eyes are left, the instrument called 'almagda', or in your left hand, if the eyes are right; then place the tip of the instrument beside the cornea with the thickness of a line in that white part of the eye at the part of the lower lid, then push the instrument called 'almagda' carefully, and turn your hand so it pierces the white of the eye, feeling that almagda reaches an empty space; and make sure that the length of the way almadga travels is exactly the depth from the top of the eyeball to its end; and this is the cornea of the eye; you will see the bone in that paper due to the clarity of the horny membrane, and then place the instrument until it reaches where the water is, then express it under a path after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the swelling goes down now, the patient will see before them and the instrument in their eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting for a moment, and if the swelling rises again, insert force with the instrument, and when it is fixed in place and does not rise, extract the almagda lightly while turning your hand back and forth; then put a little seal gem stone ointment on the eye.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then place over the eye with dry lint or wet wool in rose oil and egg white, and bind it with a healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those of our time, put on it crushed cumin with plenty of egg white.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almagda cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, for there are some men who have very hard eyes, then you must take the instrument called 'alberit', of which this is the shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And therefore pierce the conjunctiva only, do not go too deep but make a subtle hole, then insert the almagda as we have said; and upon completion of this procedure provide for the patient an attractive bed where they may sleep on their back in a dark place; avoid all movement, take light food, and do not move their head to either side, be bound according to your discretion for three days; unbind them in that same dark room, test their vision, make them see some things, then re-bind the wound until the seventh day; it is not fitting to do this during or after the incision at present but you must ease up on this so as not to raise the water.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	If an abscess appears, do not unbind the eye before the seventh day, and treat it with a poultice to ease the abscess; when it is healed, uncover the eye and apply gold leaf to cover for one day, then return them to that dark room.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then leave the house step by step, and turn towards your quarters; know that no disciple should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And a man came to us from Iran, who told us that in his country they make pierced alembics, from which water is extracted, but I have never seen any such thing in our land, nor have I read about it in the books of the ancients; perhaps this is something new.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of alembic forms, for those who do not know them to see; and they are properly made of copper.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And the head is of the same subtle material, and the end is in three angled corners.
de la char sor le neis	Of flesh above the nose.
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes there are born flesh bumps of different kinds, some which resemble scorpions with many feet; and if there be such with flesh raised in colored spots, and if it has soft flesh of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	With this soft flesh that is not raised, you must make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; and open their nostrils, and take out the old skin of these bumps, and treat them with a strong ointment; then cut off what you can bear with a thin sharp spatula until you know that all the flesh is removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if any remains that cannot be cut off, then open it up all over with delicate instruments lightly so that nothing is left; and if this does not overcome you, or the wound becomes hot, then treat the patient as required; and if these are malignant abscesses, hurry and cauterize until the blood ceases to flow and all flesh is removed, then apply an astringent and wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the nose bleeds and moisture reaches the palate, know that it is healing; and if the moisture does not pierce as it should, know that there is cartilage in the bone above, preventing the instruments from cutting: then you must insert a piece of linen thread, slightly thicker, knotted at one end, with a space of about an inch or less between each knot; have the patient place the head of the nose on the thread to its fullest extent and draw it out by pulling gently until it emerges through the nostril into the mouth; children in schools often do this, and it is a simple thing for those who wish to perform it; then hold one end that comes through the nostril with one hand, and the other end that emerges from the mouth with the other hand, and know each extremity by feeling along the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this so that you know the night has corrupted that flesh, then draw out the son, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread with Egyptian ointment, and replace it back into the nose as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointments have eroded all remaining flesh; and then insert a cane of lead for some days until it is healed, and if there's need for drying medicines, use them; and that's the shape of the instrument to purge the head, through which oils and medicines are distilled into the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And let it be made of silver or copper, resembling an open lamp, like a pipe, and it also conducts thus; and if you wish, make a closed pipe, and let the instrument be full to purge the head; and hold one handle on the head to keep it steady when heating oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	from the flesh above the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Often a disease arises on the head of the nose called 'telul', and it grows and becomes large over time, becoming an unsightly thing to behold; therefore, you must cut it out at the beginning, and remove it entirely, then apply either a cauterizing agent or burning medicine; if one waits too long until it is large, take heed if it is hard, of dark color, and devoid of feeling: do not touch it with iron, for it is an abscess that has developed, because when one cuts into it, great harm comes to the patient; if the abscess is soft to the touch, not of a dark hue, and you see that it can be wholly cut out, then empty the patient's bowels and cut it without fear, cleansing the wound with drying and constrictive agents.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when the operation of continuing into one of these cartilaginous works yields little benefit, except for some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary then that when this happens to anyone, consider if the wound is fresh and has all its blood; and then join the two lips in a suture, then treat it until it heals; and if the lips are already separated on both sides, you must remove all the parts of their heart until they bleed, then bring together the two lips in a suture, hold them, and apply powder of dragon's blood and ground incense over the powders; place upon the powders a piece of strong emplastrum or another sealing plaster, and leave it until it scars by itself, then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of sewing is such that you unite the edges: either with needles, as we have said for suturing the abdomen; or with thread, as I have made you aware.
des apostemes des levres	Of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Skilled men find within the lips hard abscesses, similar to grains of wheat, both small and large; you must then turn back the lip, make an incision over each one, take hold with forceps, and cut into its every part; afterwards fill the place with powdered vitriol until the blood is stanched; later clean it easily, and treat the area with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	On the flesh of the gums.
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.
