Many times a fleshy growth arises on the gums, which the ancients call 'albulus'; you must grasp it with forceps, cut into its base and let the pus or blood flow out; then apply ground vitriol or other drying and cauterising powders to the wound; if this flesh returns after incision - as it often does - remove it a second time and cauterise: it will not return after the cautery; these are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	Of sores.
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes hard crusts are found at the top of teeth inside the mouth between the gums which are ugly and rough, sometimes also the teeth go black or yellow-green with putrefaction reaching the gum so that the tooth stinks; you must seat the patient in your lap and hold his head steady with one hand while with the other you extract these crusts from between his teeth - all of them - as well as the decayed parts, whether they are dark green or yellow or any other colour until no trace remains. And do this again on the second day if necessary, and also on the third so that everything is removed; know that for cleaning teeth various tools must be used depending upon what work needs to be done since scrapers which clean the outside of the tooth have a different shape from those that reach inside it; these shapes and others should all be available.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat the tooth of its pain that you delay in extracting it as much as you can, because this should not be done; for it is a very important substance until such time as one has no excuse to remove it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is forced to extract (the tooth), you must be certain of which tooth is causing pain.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the pain troubles the patient, and they believe it is in a healthy tooth, leading to the extraction of a good tooth; yet the pain does not subside because the bad one remains, as we have seen with these sinners; and when you are certain which tooth is causing pain, you must scrape around the tooth entirely with a strong spatula to protect the gum on all sides; then hold it in your two hands or with subtle pincers at the first pit and cavity, until it is well loosened, then firmly grip the pincers; and have the patient's head resting healthily between your knees, holding it steady so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it cannot be removed, use one of these instruments and gently insert them on each side, moving it as you did initially.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	If the tooth is perforated and worn down, you must fill it with small pieces of cloth where there are holes; then carefully extract it with forceps, ensuring it does not break during extraction; it requires great skill to work around the gum to remove the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	Be careful not to break the tooth, leaving a part of it behind, as this will cause the patient even greater pain due to the remaining root.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	Beware of not doing as the ignorant surgeons do, who in their haste and boldness sometimes break the jaw, and fail to address what we have described; they sometimes cause severe illness due to remaining roots or a broken jaw, as we have often seen; once the tooth is removed, clean the area with wine or oil and silk; if there is bleeding, fill the space with crushed vitriol; and if this does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the instruments, with which you first loosen the teeth, should have long points and thick handles so that they do not bend when you pull the tooth. These are the tools needed:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should have thick shafts so that they do not bend when pulling, and be well-made iron with teeth to grip the tooth.
de la racine des dens	From the root of the teeth.
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains during extraction, you must place moist cotton soaked in butter over the socket for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the socket softens, you can insert pincers called "algefri", which look like a stork's beak; their shape is that of a file with teeth inside, this is how they should be made:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not wish to come out with all these tongs, then you must uncover the flesh all around the root, and place the instrument which is called 'althali', that is to say, a scalpel, of which this is the form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root comes out by this means, it is good; if not, assist with all the instruments, of which the forms are as follows:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one requires assistance with this instrument, which has two blades, of which the form is as follows:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other iron instruments that are positioned at the root of the teeth, and of this instrument which resembles large tongs, of which the form is as follows:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let this instrument be strong enough so that it cannot break; and know that there are many dental instruments, along with other types of tools which aren't included here; and wise master craftsmen find their own tools by themselves according to the jobs they do and the illnesses they treat, because there are such diverse diseases that ancient authors did not teach any instrument for them; if you don't break the skull or the other bones where it could be damaged, then look for the instruments which I have said suit you, and help yourself with gestures, of which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	They should be thick and secure enough to hold the bone so that it doesn't escape, but can still be held and removed; then restore the place with medicines appropriate for this purpose, and if there is rot in the bone, and it is small, then remove all of these instruments.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear not according to their natural form, and they are ugly, especially in virgin women, you must know if the tooth is newly born after another one, and it is not in its right place, and cannot be treated or filed: then extract it; and if it is connected with a tooth, take this instrument which has the following shape, similar to a small beak, and made of iron sharpened at the end.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And strike it several times with a hammer during the day for its hardness, and so that you do not move other teeth, and if it is apparent that it can be filed, then file it with this kind of rasp whose shape resembles this.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	which is also similar to the rasp used for making needles; and file the tooth several times during the day lightly, so that it does not move until you finish filing completely with any kind of small rasp, and if the tooth is too sharp and hurts the tongue, then you must file its roughness enough to make it even, so that it doesn't hurt the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	When teeth loosen
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When front teeth loosen due to impact or fall, and the patient cannot bite down without them falling out, even after treatment with constricting medicines which is ineffective, they must be restrained with a gold wire, as silver wire turns green and decays but gold does not change; and let the wire be neither too thin nor too thick according to the space between the teeth; and if you wish to straighten the teeth, take the wire and pass it double through two healthy teeth, then place the loose tooth or teeth between them until you have reached safely to a sound tooth on the other side; then repeat the covering process back to where you started, drawing your hand carefully and gently so as not to move anything, and let your binding be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then cut the gums of the thread with a pair of pliers, and gather them together, and fasten them between the healthy tooth and the tongue, placing it so that it does not wound the tongue; then leave it thus tightly bound as long as it can remain, and if it loosens or the thread breaks, tighten it with another thread; if it remains in place and serves its purpose, this is the method for fixing two healthy teeth, and two loose ones, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth falls out, one places it back in its position, fresh for fresh, as we have said; and let no one who is not wise and skilled be involved, and sometimes the shape of a tooth is made from cow bone, and placed where the gap is, and tightened as we have described, and it remains thus serving for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cut loose the tongue's bond
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	This ligament sometimes arises beneath the tongue by nature, or through an accident of a healed wound; and the operations are such that you open the patient's mouth, have their head in your lap, and lift up their tongue; then cut loose the broad nervous ligament, so that the tongue is released from its bond, and if there is hardness or knot, which comes suddenly after a wound, thrust in the hook and cut widely this ligament; take care that the incision is not too deep, for the artery beneath; and when you have done this, wash the place with rose water and egg white, or cold water, then put under the tongue a tent of linen; and the patient must hold each night so that the wound cannot heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	If bleeding occurs, apply crushed vitriol to the site immediately. If blood continues to flow, cauterize with a small-spot cautery, which is suitable for this purpose; then treat it further until it heals completely.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you notice it becomes discolored to green or black and hard, so the patient does not feel it, do not touch as this is cancer. If there is a decline towards whitening and moisture present, incise with an lancet and open it up gently with a slender spatula; then drain from one end to another until all matter has been released. When blood flow occurs during your procedure, apply ground vitriol until the bleeding stops completely before returning to your task so as not leave any remainder within afterwards. Finally treat this area separately using other treatments until healed thoroughly thereafter.
des apostemes de la gorge	abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes abscesses form inside the throat called "godath," which are properly known as the two tonsils; and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, if they do not heal, take care: if it is a hard abscess with a small base and light color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron, also for the discharge of blood; but leave it until it matures, then you can remove it, or it will break open on its own; and if it is white with clear roots, prepare your instruments to cut, but first check whether the abscess has cooled down and is soothed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, and ses chiés soit en ton sain, 
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	When you press the tongue against all this instrument, and you see the abscess, then take the lancet and fix it in the almond, and pull it upwards as much as you can; and draw out any threads with it, then cover the instrument, of which this is the shape, that seems like a forceps; and nonetheless its heads are bent, and one against the other, and they are very sharp, and it is made of iron or steel.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this instrument ready, then cover it with the tongs, of which this is the shape:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And let it be sharp on one side and blunt on the other; and when you have covered one of the almonds, then cover the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with warm water, and water mixed with alum, and if blood flow occurs, then gargle the patient with water or with boiled pomegranate rinds, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding is stopped; then treat it until it is healed; and sometimes other abscesses occur in the throat besides the two almonds, so treat them likewise as you would the two almonds.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that had formed inside her throat, specifically a small abscess; it had nearly closed off her entire throat, so the woman could not breathe through the blocked passageway, nor could she eat or drink, and she would have died if she remained like this for even one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	The abscess was so swollen that it had burst, with two streams of pus escaping through the nostrils.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I then quickly grabbed hold and inserted a spike into one nostril, forcing it through, and extracted a large piece of bowel through the other nostril; I pushed this piece back in through the other nasal passage, opened up her mouth, and pressed on her tongue; after that, I inserted the spike into the abscess and cut away part of it, removing only a small amount of blood; thus, the throat's passageway was unblocked for the woman, who could now drink water and then wine, and ceased not to drain this abscess over an extended period; the abscess would heal and fill the space I had emptied until it became very large again; at that point, I cauterized it within her throat: thus halting its growth. And so she remained, without further increase in size or severity of symptoms. I then left these parts behind, trusting God to take care of the patient from there on out.
de l’uve	Of the eye.
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the membrane descends to the eye, and it is swollen and elongated, it is called a "perpendicular"; if it is below, thick, and round, it is called an "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit, and you see that the sore abscesses are alleviated, and it is subtle, then you must cut it; and if it is a round mass and not elongated, and it is bloody or of false colour or black, then you should avoid incising it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is necessary, therefore, when you see it according to the manner I have described, regarding its whiteness and length, that you make the patient sit facing the sun, and press their tongue with the instrument which we previously mentioned; then insert the needle into the eye, draw it down, and cut it using one of two instruments I mentioned for the incision of almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you must not cut away any more flesh than the superfluity that lies beyond nature's boundary; for if you cut more, it will cause harm to the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient fears cutting, you must employ an engine for cauterization to ease their fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is quicksilver.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And have the patient put their head in your lap, then press their tongue with the instrument we mentioned in the chapter on cauterization, and seal it with hot quicksilver, but not too thick or too thin; and use this tool for its purpose, of which the form is thus:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; 
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cauterization; if it is cured by fumigation according to this method, take calmament and hyssop and oregano and rue and chamomile and vervain and similar herbs, and mix all or some of them in one pot, add oil, and boil it; the pot should be well glazed with strong clay, and inside the pot have one instrument shaped like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be made of silver or copper, and one end of the instrument is inserted into the patient's mouth so that the vapor rises to the eye through the nose, until the eye becomes withered; then repeat this often, until the eye dries up, and make sure you do not perform this at the beginning of the occurrence of a hot abscess, as many things may happen; and do not carry out this procedure when the hot abscess is declining.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a cane and put a piece of egg shell inside the patient's mouth so that it does not get too hot; for the eggshell will not let the vapour harm the mouth, and it is a good remedy together with safety.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Often something sticks in the throat - a fish bone or some object; therefore, you must take out what you can see, and press the tongue under sunlight towards the entire instrument so that you may observe movement of the object; and for that which does not appear to you and remains stuck in the throat, it is necessary that you make the patient vomit before the food is digested in the stomach; perhaps in this way the object will come out with the vomiting; or let the patient swallow a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel (umbilical cord), or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread; and tie to the sponge a thread, then let it be swallowed; when it reaches the place, it will stick out, and then you can pull it out; if it does not come out by what we have said, take an instrument made of lead in this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instruments be curved at the tip so that they can more easily enter the throat, and keep the head raised upwards; guard against touching the epiglottis, lest it swell, nor push any bone inside; better that the patient pushes the instrument himself, for he knows best where the problem is located; if you insert it down, or pull it out through his mouth, do so gently with equal force all over, until it is completely removed.
de la sansue de la gorge	from the phlegm of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	In no case is phlegm medicinal, as I said in the division of cures; and when it does not benefit, then examine the patient's throat under sunlight, then press their tongue with an instrument that I told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the leech, draw it out with a very small hook, or use delicate forceps that are suitable for this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this does not work, take a hair from the tail of a horse, insert it into the patient's throat, then attach a hot iron to the end of the hair, and repeat this frequently.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient has water retention all day long.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full glass of cold water and open the patient's mouth, pour it in so they swallow it, and keep hold of them by their hand frequently; as soon as the leech feels the water, it will fall out.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not fall out as we have said, then smoke the patient with asafetida, using the instrument I mentioned for fumigating the eye; do this many times, for it will fall without delay.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the manner of the fumigation is such that you take a pot with visible coals, and cover it with a perforated lid in the middle, and place the end of the instrument through this hole; then throw your fumigation into it, and let the patient put the head of the cane in their mouth, closing the mouth so that no smoke escapes but goes down to the lungs; and the lungs will now discharge phlegm, and if they do not discharge it, restart the fumigation several times; and let the patient feel thirsty, eating salty things and similar, drinking no water; then there is a need for them to cough up phlegm through this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which we extract phlegm is such that when it can be seen, it resembles bent tongs to insert into the throat; and has a resemblance to a bird's beak, and has the roughness of a file, so that what it grasps, it cannot let go; and see here its form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	There are many types of abscesses according to what memory brings forth in this book from one and another, they vary in perforation and size; there are two kinds one is by its very appearance itself, and because of moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second kind is according to their location in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For abscesses of the head are different from those of the fundament, and abscesses in fleshy places are different from those that come to joints, and each has its own treatment.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And one must not pierce abscesses when the bowels are dead according to their completion; and for those which need piercing when they are ripe, and do not die according to their completion, like abscesses near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses develop near joints, and one leaves it until it rots all around, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, which is why this causes contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	When the abscess is located near the main limb, and if you delay perforating it until it dies, it will harm the principal limb; when it is near the foundation, pierce it before it dies; and you must not puncture an abscess created without digestion being complete, unless that which is near the foundation rots entirely, forms a fistula, and cannot heal for a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you must know the time for perforating and draining the dead abscess according to its development, which is when the pain subsides, the fever breaks, and there is a reduction in pain, redness, swelling, and tenderness of the head of the abscess, as well as other signs; and you should make an incision at the lowest point of the abscess where it appears raised, and this perforation must be along the length of the body, but if the abscess is on the hands or feet, near a joint, nerve, or artery, then in all equal places with no curvature.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those that bend, according to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when the abscess is in fleshy tissue, it is better that you allow the perforation to remain until it is confirmed as healed by complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it before that, the body of the poison would be elongated and full of much dirt; and by chance, the lips may harden and the depth of it will close up.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And for any abscess that is pierced according to the breadth of the body, according to what the member requires.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you must make small abscesses with small perforations; and in large abscesses, large perforations, and many incisions according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and for such abscesses where it is necessary to cut into the heart, one should do so when it becomes like a piece of cloth, and has softened, then you must act as with boils: and there are some that have three angles, and others which are cut like myrtle leaves, like abscesses from carbuncles; and those where one makes a circular incision, other incisions, and similar cuttings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; 
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the spirits sometimes twitch with the exit of the bowels, which by chance may kill the patient, and you won't realize it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, dry the wound, and observe if the abscess wound is small; and if it's a full-blown sore, apply linen or old cotton threads; and if it's a large abscess with many perforations, you must insert a thread into each so that they come together; and if you've cut away part of the skin around the abscess, fill it with old cotton or shaved flax cloth without moisture, and bind it until the third day; then remove it, and clean it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if there is bleeding during your procedure, bring cold and light water, dampen the cloths, and place them on the bleeding area multiple times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the bleeding persists, apply compresses and ointment, and use the powders I mentioned earlier in this book, on different areas as required. If it is winter and the area or abscess is very sensitive, you should put warm tents and cloths dampened with wine and oil; if it is summer and the area is fleshy, use cloths dampened with water and oil, or cold wine and oil, for up to three days, as we have said; then uncover the abscess, wipe it, and treat it appropriately until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this must be known universally for treating abscesses: now I have told you how one should proceed to treat abscesses, and here is the chapter (on that).
des soros	abscesses
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where the skull of the head is soft come small abscesses, and they are like cloth, similar to the inside of a hen's egg, and there are many such things (abscesses).
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	Some are fatty and such that they have moisture like pus; and of such there are those which are hard and stony to cut into, and there is no doubt if the arteries do not act contrary (to treatment).
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of cutting is such that you must test every instrument which is called an "entromissoire", from which its form comes afterwards, what thing it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if there is moisture present, they do so above the long bone.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is evacuated, thoroughly scrape away without leaving any skin where this moisture was present, for it will return if nothing is left behind; then apply a dressing of cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, if available; if not, use water and salt, pack the wound, and leave it until the next day; these procedures will expel whatever remains from the night before.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that, resume the cotton dressing as before on the second day, and on the third, until you know for sure that nothing remains from the night before; then treat the wound with an appropriate ointment, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds in fatty tissue, incise it in this manner, from the long bone; insert your fingers, and scrape out all the pus, and apply all your treatment to drawing out the core where it lies; but if an artery opposes you, then do as I told you before.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also of the abscess if it is full, and of cutting and treating as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the incision on the full abscess and moisture is lighter, as they have little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if for some of these abscesses or head where there is no moisture, and in this case the abscess which I opened from an old woman's head; and found it like a hard stone, rough and white, and could not be crushed; and if one were to cut into it, they would also cause as much injury as with a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming from the head, especially those which appear on children's heads and at the roots of ears, they should always be opened as low as possible so that pus may flow out; and treat them as is needed.
des scrophules	scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Often these abscesses occur on the neck, and beneath the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes elsewhere on the body, and they are numerous, and connected to each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly within its own compartment, just like the brain and head abscesses we have mentioned, and there are many similar cases of these scrofulas.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are malignant ones that do not want to obey the rules of health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	So for those that you see are of a good nature when touching them, and appear similar in color to the body, and move with each movement yet are not near the neck veins or arteries nor the passageway, and it is not deep; then you must cut it from above, and peel off its skin on all sides, and extend the two lips of the heart as needed, just like we have said for head abscesses; remove it piece by piece, and be sure that you do not cut any nerves or veins, and ensure your spatula is blunt and unsharpened so the contents don't escape, and don't dig too deeply lest you cut something you mustn't.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery and it will not stop operating, so put in the wound ground glass, or certain powders that stanch blood, and hold the wound; and leave it until the abscess is appeased, and the wound is softened, and it begins to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the blood is staunched, then return to your work until you complete it; then look with your right index finger if there remains any small scrofulae, so cut and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large wound in the root of the scrofula, then it must not be cut at its root, but tied with a strong double thread, and left to drop by itself without harm; then dress the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then heal it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you remove the entire scrofula, then you must bring together the two lips of the wound, and suture them now, given that there has been no delay in treating the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	you must proceed to cut the root of it, and draw out the humors, and suture it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For those scrofula that have excess tissue, pierce where it is soft and putrefying; and pierce it in the same way as mentioned before, depending on its type, then apply dressings with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, treat it with an ointment that promotes flesh growth until it heals.
de squinance	of dislocation
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke of the incision in the throat; but I have never seen it performed in our land, and this is a record of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those with dislocation, it is necessary to ensure that the incision in the throat, known as the epiglottis, is avoided; and one should not perform aid in this way, because all the veins and pores of the patient are vulnerable to those who have an abscess hot in the mouth, or in the throat or in both tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the channel of the pore, it is necessary to cut the epiglottis to escape the destruction that comes from suffocation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is necessary, therefore, when we wish to split the epiglottis, that we split it below three circles or four with a small transverse slit between two circles or according to the quantity of the incision of the surface, not in the cartilage; and these are suitable for the section of the epiglottis where there is no flesh, and the vessels are long from within.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is afraid, one must extend the skin of the throat throughout, then split the heart until it reaches the windpipe; and remove the vessels of blood, if you see anything, and then cut the surface as we have said; and it is proven by the section of the breath of the windpipe that it should be through the place which is broken, and by the fault of the voice; and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed that one suspects strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound from the heart, and cut it completely without the cartilage; then administer medicines that promote flesh growth until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Al-Bukhari states that one should not do this until the throat is completely blocked, and the patient is judged to be dying, and breathing becomes impossible.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then make an incision on the epiglottis so that the patient can breathe, and they will be saved from death; for this reason, the ancients advised leaving the wound open until the evil of the disease has passed, and it passes in three or four days. Then they would order to stitch up the wound and treat it until it was healed; I shall tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a damsel took a knife and plunged it into her throat, severing part of the windpipe; I was called to treat her, but she appeared dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound and found blood flowing from it; I knew she had not cut a vein or damaged her lungs, but air was escaping through the injury.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hastened to sew up the wound and treated it until it was healed; other than her being hoarse, the damsel suffered no further harm and returned to full health; thus do I say that in epiglottis injuries there is no need for fear.
de la grosse gorge	Of the swollen throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "gorge hernia," and it's a large abscess with a yellowish colour; it is quite common in women; and occurs in two ways: naturally or accidentally; where there are no internal injuries.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	The accident occurs in two ways, one resembling our fat tissue, and the other resembles an abscess originating from an artery; and there is fear involved, and cauterization with fire should not be done except in small cases, examine and probe thoroughly: if you find it similar to our fatty tissue, and unable to access any veins, then cut it like we cut a nail, remove its entire covering if necessary; probe carefully, and treat as required until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	Des nous
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to treat the shoulder, that you first examine and inquire about all the instrument which is called an 'entromissoire', according to how its form will appear in the following chapter.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the way of inquiring about new abscesses is that you take hold of the moistest part which you find in the abscess, and turn your fingers back and forth until you know the instrument has pierced the core, then do so according to the size of the abscess; then withdraw the entromissoire, taking care not to damage it.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If running moisture is present, regardless of its colour, treat it as I have said for other abscesses; and if after the entromissoire there is no moisture, know that it is fatty, so cut it in a cross shape, take pincers to pull on it gently from each side, and use the shoulder blade where it lies to scrape it healthy with the entromissoire; and if you cannot make it healthy, then remove it by pieces until nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if anything remains there, the pus returns many times; and if a little bit is left behind, and it causes you grief, then fill the wound with some sharp corrosive powders, constrict the wound, and place warm abscess-soothing substances on it, cure it with other cures until it heals; and if the pus is large, cut the two lips of the wound, and cure it with something that produces flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the throbbing vein opposes you or something else hastes you, apply crushed vitriol to it, and leave it there for two or three days until the wound becomes gangrenous, and halts the boiling of blood; then return to cut away what remains from last night.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here are the shapes of the insertion instruments, and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small; and there are three squares called "albaret", and one called "breb"; and they come in three sizes: large, medium, and small, for probing abscesses or fistulas; also like needles that we use to sew up sores, they are made of yellow brass, iron, or silver, yet those which are yellow are better, and more tried-and-true black lead is used to probe the curves of a fistula; and these come in three sizes: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of the uncinas are very diverse, as you can see here: large, medium, and small; and there are uncinas with two curves in three different ways; and there are uncinas with three curves, also in three different ways; and there are uncinas with two curves, and some with only one curve, again in three different ways; and all these types are necessary for their purpose.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The heads of these instruments are sharp for cutting purposes and there are some that only cut on one side, which we use to slice open skin without damaging the nerves; the introduction of this instrument is carefully done in many places so as not to alarm the patient when opening abscesses; they come in three different sizes: large, small, and medium, as you can see here; it should never be used on fleshy areas such as legs, arms, breasts, or similar places; sometimes a smaller variation of this instrument is made resembling skin-scrapers for staunching blood, according to the following shape.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is placed back into position to heal by compression of the veins, arteries, and sometimes according to this large form.
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to deteriorate, making them resemble female breasts; they remain unsightly and swollen, and if one wishes to treat them, it is necessary to follow this procedure from point b. to g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	scrape away the fat, treat the wound with medicated flesh-building ointment, then bring together the two lips of the wound with stitches, treating it until it is healed; and if the breast sags downwards, softened by its size as happens in women, make an incision dividing it into two lobes above, through two similar clefts; so that one is attached to the other at the end of each, such that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from point b. to g.; then scrape away the skin which lies between the two lips, remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitches and powders, and what is necessary for treatment, until it is healed; if it is not healed or the incision is not completely made, because of patient reluctance to rest, or due to loss of blood, you must pack the wound with wet cotton in corrosive ointment; leave this in place until it discharges any remaining fat tissue, then treat it until it is fully healed.
des apostemes des asselles	Of abscesses under the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses which come from under the armpits are like hard scrofulae when they have sides, and if there is moisture contained within them.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those which contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line b. to line g.
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the matter within the abscess is evacuated, fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day; then remove all the cotton, and dress it gently until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess resembles a scrofula, treat it as we have said for scrofulae incisions; and if the wound is deep, apply cauterization as mentioned before.
de la routure de l’artere	From the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is ruptured, and the skin above it is welded together, abscesses often form, and similarly, the vein becomes swollen and abscessed; one recognizes this for the artery when the abscess runs lengthwise perfectly; and if you feel it with your fingers, there will be a constriction; and where it belongs to the vein, its prominence appears round; and it is foolishness to cut into this abscess, especially when it lies beneath the axilla and breast, or neck and other places, and is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	One must therefore avoid the iron cure, and in that which is at the head one should also avoid it, and in that of arterial swelling, make an incision above the skin lengthwise; then cut open the wound with scissors, and carefully separate the artery from its membranes until it is exposed; then insert a needle underneath it, pierce through to the other side, and secure the artery with double thread at two points, according to what I have taught you for the extraction of the two arteries in the temples; then seal up the area between the two ligatures with an intrument so that blood which is there may flow out, and open up the abscess; then apply a cure made from raw bow gut so as to allow the ligature to fall off; finally treat the place where the abscess was until it heals; and if the abscess is caused by cutting of the vein, one must hold with his hand whatever can be held of the abscess and all the skin around it, then insert a needle underneath what you have in your hand, piercing through, and having double thread, so that you draw it out from the other side; next secure the abscess as I told you, by ligatures on either end of two sections of thread; and if you fear that this will not hold, you reinsert another needle with all the thread underneath the entire abscess to the incision of the first needle, then tighten the threads in four places; then cut open the abscess so that its superfluities flow out, after which clean the core of the excess, leaving what is tied; then apply a moist cloth soaked in wine and oil, finally treat it with bandages and ointments until healed.
des apostemes des ners	Of abscesses of nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Likewise abscesses come to the arteries and veins, abscesses come to the nerves when they are torn, or due to excessive heavy labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And these occur more frequently in the shoulders and hands and everywhere there are joints, and this is a serious abscess, and its color resembles that of the body, and it appears in various places without pain; when one grasps it firmly, the patient feels pain, and it is not on the surface of the body but below the heart; it moves well from all sides, neither forward nor backward, neither above nor below, and the abscess which is in joints should not be cut with iron: perhaps contraction would occur; and that which is on the head or forehead, one must open with a spatula.
