Cela se produit en raison de l'extension du syfac dans les intestins, comme nous l'avons dit, car il est étendu, puis le lieu de la blessure s'adoucit et s'ouvre ; et le traitement consiste en un cautère, comme nous l'avons déjà dit; parfois, cela est traité avec un fer de cette manière : le patient repose souvent sur son dos entre tes mains, tu coupes alors le lieu de la rupture enflé dans une largeur correspondant à trois doigts ; ensuite, retire le syfac qui se trouve sous la peau que tu as ensuit; prends ensuite le rait et place-le sur l'endroit apparent du syfac; presse le au fond du ventre, puis coupe les deux endroits apparents du syfac situés au dessus de la tête du rait, en coupant d'un côté puis de l'autre ; ensuite retire la tête du rait, mais ne coupe aucunement du syfac ou n’étends pas l'œuf ni autre chose, comme je te l'ai expliqué dans le traitement de la ramice des intestins; ensuite traite-le par le traitement des plaies.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the sons' hairs, clean them thoroughly and treat the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The surgeon is compelled to act; there are no signs of healing in the wound, and cauterization here is necessary for recovery.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	from softening the skin of the calves
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Often the skin of the calves is softened in certain people because the fat beneath has become soft and visible, and it needs to be removed if you wish to treat it; place the patient on their back for this procedure, then cut away the softened skin from healthy skin, bring together the two edges with a suture, and if you wish, stitch the superfluous part of the softened skin with three or four strong sutures; then cut between the sutures and treat like other wounds until it is healed.
dou chastrement	L'amputation
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Know that amputations are prohibited by our law, and for this reason I would prefer not to discuss them in this book; it is only necessary for two reasons: one being so that the doctor can answer questions when asked about it and know the cure; and the other because we often need to perform amputations on some animals to help us, such as goats, sheep, cats and other beasts.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say that amputations are done in two ways: either by traction or by incision.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the case of amputations done by traction, we make the animal sit in warm water until its tendons are softened and relaxed; then you grasp them with your hand so they can be removed without feeling it.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Du chastrement de taille: it is necessary that you hold the animal and press its testicles with your left hand, then tie a suspending cord around them, and cut each of them with one stroke when they are well-scrotched; leave some of the skin where the sinews and delicate sinews which are on the vessels are located; this type of castration is more deadly than that done by extraction because there may remain in this case something from the testicles so that the animal continues to feel lust, then heal the wound until it is cured.
des hermofrodites	Il sont bestes monstrueus qui ont les deux membres et ont la vertu de copuler comme l’omme et la femme, ce sont por ceu des bestes impures et abominables.
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	An hermaphrodite can be of two kinds among men: one is when between the two testicles appears as if it were a woman's body part with hair and sometimes urine comes out.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And this other type [of dislocation] occurs in women, affecting the wrist like a rod and with two knobs.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	The treatment of both men and women is such that you must cut away all the damaged flesh, and treat it like other wounds; in the second type [of dislocation], where the urine escapes through the skin of the knobs, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	Of tensioning.
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Tensioning is damaged flesh on the natural part of the body, so ugly to look at that some women have it as large as a hand, and this requires treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	You must hold the excess of tensioning with your hand or pincers, and cut it lightly; do not go too deep lest blood flow from it, then treat any other damaged flesh until it is healed; there is another type of tissue that grows at the mouth of the wound, filling it, perhaps like a cow's udder, so the ancients called this "udder disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	You must cut it off, as we have said with tendonitis, and treat it until it is healed.
de erratique	Of erratics
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratic is the case when the nature of a woman's opening is not perceived or is small; and it is natural by birth, an accident due to illness, caused by scar tissue from a subtle wound or species, and is made perfect in the marriage bed, whether on her back, side, or elsewhere; it prevents conception, childbirth, and perhaps flowers [the monthly period]; knowledge of this is obtained through observation of the bath.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the obstruction is close to the surface, take it with your fingers or a rod.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If he is delicate and near the two lips, hasten to treat it thus: place your two index fingers together, and have the woman lie on her back with legs spread; then stretch the two lips wide apart so that the delicate wound is exposed, and cover the stitches; then take wool, moisten it in oil, and place it on the site, having the woman lie with a man each day, such that it cannot heal.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the wound is hard and thick, you must cut it with a spatula similar to myrtle leaves.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the stitches are of new wood, suspend them with horsehair and cut it; and have on hand medicines that stop bleeding, such as dragon's blood, incense, mixed with egg white; then apply a wide piece of lead foil so that the wound cannot heal; and thus it will be long-lasting, and bring her a tent of dry linen; then treat any other injuries until she is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when a tumor develops in the womb, it should be removed in this manner, unless there are embedded abscesses.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For the abscess that is embedded in the womb, one should not attempt any treatment involving fire.
des emorroides	Hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that usually bleed, and when hemorrhoids are old they become hard; we have previously mentioned their similarities to other conditions, and the signs, and now I will tell you which ones can be cured.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and hard tumors, when they are perfectly located in the anus and do not protrude, should not be treated with fire.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the mare's [illness], one can feel, are those that can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	You must therefore put the woman in a cold house, then extend the ulcer with tongs, and cut it at its roots, then powder on medicine that constricts blood, such as dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then press her feet against the wall for an hour, then put her into cold water; and if there is still bleeding, make her sit in a decoction of sumac, pomegranate rind, galls, and similar things, and then take barley flour, mix it with honey and egg white, and make an ointment on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stops bleeding, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, let the patient drink air through cupping glasses on their back and breasts without wounding them; then take wool, dampen it in juice of plantain or elderberry with old wine, and apply to the affected area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Once an abscess is healed, treat the area with ointment until it is cured; and this one called "albathir" is red, and resembles a rough head, so you must cut as I said for the carbuncle; and then treat until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	Abscesses of the cheek
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many types of abscess arise in the cheek, such as cancer, stone-filled abscess, herpes, shingles, fistulas, haemorrhoids and hot abscess, along with numerous other diseases that I have mentioned in my classification.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is therefore necessary that I speak in this treatise of the hot abscess which appears on the armpit, which is not one of those abscesses that are caused by a blow; and if you want to know how to treat it, look to see if the abscess is acute at its onset, full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red when you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Do not hasten to pierce it, but let it die until the pain subsides; then have the patient sit on a seat, and place two small seats where they lean, supporting their back and bringing their legs close to the outside of their thighs; their hips should be spread apart, and they should put their arms under their knees, binding them well with a good bandage; then suck out the matter towards the right side, and introduce the instrument used for opening the armpit, which will later take on this shape; when introducing this instrument, you must first mark out the depth of the armpit so that whatever part of the instrument goes in does not go deeper than it should, lest it hurt the patient; if the instrument is too large, then line the bottom of the armpit with cloth so that the instrument doesn't cause pain; they must hold the end of the instrument with a funnel, holding the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess opens, and you break it with your hand gently, you must cut towards its head or spatulate edge; and when the bowels are empty, you should place in the wound moistened bandages soaked in rose oil or dry green oil; then put a cloth outside of the wound onto the skin, and on top of that place clean, moist woolen cloth with water or cooked mallow leaves; afterwards cure after II days from applying this, until it is healed; and sometimes lift up the skin and the wound with an enema of water and honey, and then with water or cooked lily roots and long aristolochia; then return to applying ointments.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is red in the flesh, you must be cautious of applying hot iron, but treat it as we have said in the previous section.
de l’enfantement	Of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	The midwife must first know the nature of childbirth and its signs, which are when you see the woman press down, and desire to smell air: then the child hastens to come out forcefully; thus know that these births follow natural order, with the issue beneath their head, and the second stage accompanying it; and when you see these signs, gently pressing her belly is necessary so the child can leave quickly; for once they descend onto its head, there's a second stage accompanying them, and the husband sees his wife rid of all superfluity by proper cleansing; those who come otherwise are not born naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For sometimes it comes out from the feet first, or forcefully from the body or shoulders, and hands; it can come from the stomach, often ending up turned around its neck, or other bad positions; thus the midwife must be wise and skilled in these matters to avoid error and disappointment, as I will show you all possible outcomes on how they should aid.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child is born head-first through natural birth, and the woman gives birth with difficulty due to her weak constitution, have her sit on a saddle or be held by women; arouse her nature with oil of fenugreek that has been cooked, then insert the small spatula into her vagina.
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	Cut the amniotic sac and trim her nail so that the moisture inside flows out; press on the woman's stomach until the child descends; if it does not descend, administer an enema of fenugreek mucilage with sesame oil to the woman; then make her sneeze from condiments, holding her mouth and nose shut for an hour: now extract the child.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if both hands are outside [the birth canal], you must gently push them back one by one; and if they cannot be pushed in, place the woman on a chair with her feet raised upwards; then lift the chair to the ground, holding the woman so she does not fall when getting up; and if the hands cannot be pushed in and the child is dead, cut off its hands with the knife mentioned before, extract the child, and reset it equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	At the child's birth from its feet.
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes out on its feet, you must pull it upwards; and then turn it over and over until it is straightened; then take one of its feet and stretch it gently.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	When it reaches the thighs, instruct them to grasp and make them sneeze hard; if it jumps so be it, God willing.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not jump as we have said, turn it over and over until it is according to its natural form.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it will be lightly done.

And if it does not come out as we have said, take some mucilage of old figs, and oil of sisymbrium, and molten gum, and grind everything in a mortar; put this mixture on the woman's nature inside and outside this ointment, then make her sit in warm water up to under her ribs; when she is wet underneath, make her wear a collar of myrrh, and place it underneath, leaving it for an hour; then have her sit on a seat, then make her sneeze and hold her mouth and nose shut, gently pressing her belly, for the child jumps now.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	Of the child's exit onto their knees

de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	Of the child's exit from the broad side, with one hand hanging out.

I must use the device to bring back the hand: if it cannot be brought back, make the woman get up and walk; if she cannot walk, let her lie on the bed, and stretch her legs strongly; then apply the medication I mentioned; and if she does not give birth, sit her on a chair, then try to retrieve the hand; and exhale the child according to their natural position, make her sneeze, and instruct her to hold herself until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	Of the child's emergence from its collarbone, let it spread its hands, with its face turned towards the back of its mother.

I agree that the nurse should hold their hand, then turn it little by little, and lift it gently; when it is level, apply a mixture of nature's moss and oil as we have said, then instruct them to move it slowly; once you have done this, make them sit on a chair, and command her to grab onto something; then make the patient sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in this same manner for all secondary dislocations
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes out in this manner for all secondary dislocations, squeeze the dislocation with your nail until all moisture is drained; and if the child falls onto their face or neck, lift them from below so they are not caught underneath, and kill the child; then push the child inside, until you have put it back correctly, and instruct the woman to grab something: then gently extract it.
de l’issue des gemelz	Of the dislocation of the hips
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four are born at once; this is not a strange occurrence, but it may happen.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	These are strange and do not live, if there are several of them; I know this, that they may be multiplied, and are separated by the surgeon who divides them, which is done at the navel; sometimes they emerge naturally like a single child, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they emerge in distress, then treat them as we have said, and let the surgeon be skilled, acting quickly and lightly with his work; and do this for their well-being.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	None are formed in the womb I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or many up to XV, and they are all shaped like a child through the measurement of the glorious blood, and it is fitting that the bailiff knows all this, for perhaps similar things may happen to him; so he must act accordingly.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the woman for a dead child in her womb, as I said in the division, and it does not come out naturally, and you are forced to perform manual work; then you must know if the woman is of sound virtue, and has no accident or fear of death; then rub the mouth of the womb with moist oils mixed with a concoction of althea and fenugreek seed and linseed, then anoint the bailiff's hands with these oils and mixtures; then insert them gently into the womb, and look for one place where he inserts his fingers so that it is suitable for this, and take care if the child is equipped to descend on its head; then place your fingers in its eyes or neck or mouth or palate or under the beard or in the armpit or near the sides, and if the descent is at the feet, insert your finger in the groin or lower abdomen; he should hold the finger with his right hand, and place the curvature between his two fingers of the left hand, and push it gently with all his force, and place the finger in any of these places that we have said until the object comes out empty; this is the shape of the finger:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then insert it into the other incision, or place a third if needed so that the extractions are equal; and then stretch them evenly from side to side, for removal, and let the incisions be toothed in order to hold them, as is shown here:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if any part remains, oil your fingers and push it into that part, then pull the other part; and if there are still points remaining, place this incision higher up and do so until it comes out entirely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	If one hand comes before the other and you cannot reset it due to tightness, then you must wrap it with a cloth until it is fully extended; cut open the skin at the wrist or ankle joint, and do likewise for the other hand and foot.

Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on their feet, then the traction is light, and the adjustments at the mouth of the womb are slight.

If it is trapped in the abdomen or pelvis, then you must extract it with fabric wrapped around your hand; and split open the abdomen or pelvis until the moisture that is there drains out; and if the other limbs are removed, and the head remains, insert your hand perfectly inside the womb, and draw it towards the mouth of the womb; then insert one or two fingers, and pull it through; and if the mouth of the womb is narrowed due to hot inflammation therein, do not exert force, but apply moist and oily things; administer plasters, and also apply warm emollients and softening agents in water.

Once this is done, proceed as we have described for hot abscesses that arise in the marrow; and if discharge of blood occurs, it should be treated with cold water compresses, restraining movement, and other treatments are applied.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose belly a child had been dead, then another was born on top of it, and the other one died as well.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess formed in the jaw, swelling until it burst open, and began to rot (or stink).
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to treat him, and I thought long about it, but could not heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a plaster of strong attraction, and an object came out, seemingly like bone, then after some days another one did too.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was greatly puzzled as to why the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it might be the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I probed the wound and extracted several bones from it until the woman's condition improved significantly. She lived with a missing part of her bowels for many years; I had never come across such a case before so I am sharing this chapter in order to help others who may find unusual cases that require medical intervention.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	To bring back the bone to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	Here comes the form of the pressor, for which one needs levers; and returning to the second joint of the two bones.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	However, the horns are more subtle than the restriction device, and they should be made of ebony or boxwood; and let the mouth of the shaft be two fingers wide, and let the edge of the wood be one finger thick, and let it be a palm and a half long; and in the middle of the two bones there will be two joints of this same wood, which are firmly attached to each other at both ends, with a length of half a palm or slightly more; and these two joints are pushed into the mouth of the bone to open when you turn the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, more subtle and lighter in its resemblance, should be made of ebony or boxwood, similar to the shape of tongs; with two jaws having two adjustments each, as you see, one palm long and two fingers wide; when you wish to open the vagina with all the instrument, have the woman sit on a bed, feet hanging down and legs spread apart, then insert the two adjusted jaws together into the vagina, and hold the head of the instrument underneath between her thighs; operate your hand with the entire device as if it were tongs evenly, according to the size you wish to open the mouth of the vagina, so that she does what she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are entirely overmounted and multiplied in their resemblances; when the doctors have them prepared, they hasten to work with them more quickly, and confer greater skill on men according to their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not despair of the instrument which you have prepared, because their need is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the midwife is delayed in childbirth, you must tell the patient to hold her breath and then make her sneeze strongly, holding your hands over her mouth and nose; if she jumps due to this, it is good.

If not, take a pot and make an opening in its cover, then put herbs that can open the mouth of the sufferer, such as rue, peppermint, aniseed, chamomile, cassia, and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, must be boiled with water over fire; then place one end of the pot's spout into the other end in the mouth of the sufferer, hold it until the vapours come inside the sufferer; then make her sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the injury is caused by a fall.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this treatment, and does not heal, instruct the nurse to wet her left hand in oil of sesame or muskroot juice, and then insert it into the body, seeking the secondin. When she finds it, she should grasp it and gently pull it straight, ensuring the wound does not tear during extraction. But she must move it lightly from side to side first, and then draw it out; this will ease its removal.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	If the opening of the wound is narrowed, we have mentioned the treatment of inducing sneezing and fumigation with herbs. And if it does not heal despite all that has been said, take care not to be hasty in pulling it out. Instead, bind what is at the mouth of the wound to the woman's thigh, then administer a clyster of tetrafarmac syrup; this will ripen and reset it, leading to healing. However, when it does ripen, there may be an unpleasant odor in the stomach and head, causing discomfort to the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	So it is necessary therefore to use appropriate fumigations for this: some of the ancients have tried fumigations with watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument with which one fumigates a woman to retain her flowers and second-course is as follows:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	It is of glass similar to a dog's and has a subtle head in its nature, with broad jaws above the fire; and let the fumigation be over coals, and leave it until it is consumed, then start another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the fundament.
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born without a perforated anus, but have one closed off with a subtle membrane: therefore it is necessary at their bath to pierce that membrane herself with her finger, and not use a pointed spatula, and be careful she does not touch it; then apply moist wool soaked in wine and oil, then treat with ointment until it heals.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will heal, insert a plank peg into the hole, and leave it there for several days; remove it when the child wants to go outdoors.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	Sometimes this healing comes suddenly from a wound or an abscess; you must cut away the callus: it should be treated as we have said about the plank peg.
de la fistule dou fondement	From the anal fistula.
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Anal fistulas are inflammation and swelling that come from beneath the anus or in the space between two parts; there is a single or multiple fistula, and when this inflammation is old, it operates, and still moist with white pus or soft scabs, and sometimes these fistulas break open; they are recognized by those who have them through egestion or flatulence when the patient defecates, and perhaps a worm jumps out.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And so for fistulas that penetrate up to the bladder, and up to halfway along the penis; reaching even as far as the hip joint, and down to the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	Then one understands the fistula piercing through to the anus, or not: and it is that you insert your index finger into the anus, and carefully place a thin needle of brass or iron into the fistula where there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is any twisting, then insert a slender tent of bronze or horsehair until you feel the tent or hair with your finger; and if you do not feel it, and no egestion, wind, nor excretion comes forth as we have said: know that it does not pierce through; so wait to treat it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula pierces through to the bladder or the urine passage, it leaks urine, and cannot be healed by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it pierces through to the hip joint, its path extends down there; if there is no tortuosity and the pain arises around that area, it should be treated with a bow-shaped instrument, and medicine or ointment cannot quickly heal it; for these penetrating fistulas, there is no cure other than surgery, and the foolish surgeons who attempt them are vain.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the case of one that is not penetrated and is not an old injury, there is hope for healing with iron, as I have proven, and it must be done by placing the patient between your hands on their back; you then lift their legs up to their hips, leaning their thighs towards their stomach; next, insert a bronze probe, or silver if it is tortuous, until you find where the probe enters.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around their anus, you must insert your index finger there; if you then feel that the tendon has been pierced; and if what you feel between your finger and thumb is soft or flesh-like, know that it has indeed passed through; do not labor under the impression that it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	It is said that one can heal some of these cases well, but it rarely happens; the help provided consists in heating the subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as mentioned before; then insert the hot iron into the fistula until you reach near the anus; do this twice or three times until you know that the faulty flesh, resembling bird feathers, is burned away; afterward treat it with moistened lint soaked in butter so that the remaining raw flesh may be removed and finally cure it with a healing ointment which joins skin to skin.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If this cannot be healed in any other way; and if you insert a tent inside, and it does not pierce all the way to the rectum, but gets stuck between your finger and the tent with a thick covering of skin or tissue, and you see the fistula through the covering of heartwood; then cut away from the beginning of the fistula, push forward towards the tent, and cauterize afterwards until reaching the top of the tent; and it will release the tent and fall out; then clean those faulty tissues that resemble a bird's feather, leaving nothing behind.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if blood rushes into you and comes between your body and the work, cauterize it with fire or with medicated paste.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For fire cautery brings together two beneficial things: namely, the burning of adjacent flesh and the stemming of blood flow and drying of moisture; then treat wet wounds with butter or ground substances until the wound exudes pus, and after the flesh is burned in the presence of pus; then treat the wound with soothing ointments that harden tough flesh, and these are dry medications.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For once it is reset, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula comes right up to the anus, and is away from the body, put your finger in the anus and ask the patient.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the swelling and find either sinew or membrane or flesh where it is close to breaking through, take action with confidence and hope by administering one of three methods: cauterize as we have said, or cut down deep, or if you can apply an ointment and treat as before; but do not go too deep lest you sever the tissue that holds the anus together so that waste comes out unwillingly. Then treat it as we have said; perhaps he will be healed, or remove this covering and clean it after cutting away from the anus by ointment or other pointed instrument; then purge this faulty flesh which is in the wound until you can; then turn your attention to restoring the wound and stopping up the fistula outside of the anus: for him a lesser evil.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are formed in this manner: it occurs when you pierce the tent with a lance in the fistula, and it is located on the side of the fundament near the skin above; then take a pierced tent at its head in this form...
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	...and insert the thread awry into it in II, and pierce the tent with the thread into the fistula until its head is reached.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is pierced through the edge of the fundament inside, then remove the thread from that hole, just as you would insert your finger into the fundament; and draw out the head of the thread, and bring the two edges together, pressing one against the other, and leave it like this for one or two days; sometimes press it occasionally until the thread cuts through those parts which are between them, and discharges pus; then treat the wound until it is healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not rupture, make it burst in every way you can if it is not too deeply embedded.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not suitable to treat a wound that deeply embedded with cauterization; and then you must cure it as we have said until it heals.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the pointed spatula used to make a fistula is very sharp on one side and not on the other; thus you do not cauterize what should not be cauterized as you can see here:
des emorroydes	For haemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Haemorrhoids are of two kinds: they can be found inside the anus, like grains of resin, and there are small ones and large ones; they emit a little blood, there may be one or several, and they protrude outside the anus at its edge; however those that are on the outside have very little moisture, and in addition to this there is either some water coloured yellow, or a bit of blood, and they are the colour of skin. The cure for those who have them inside the anus is as follows: you must instruct the patient to strain themselves going into chambers until the haemorrhoids protrude from the rectum; once visible, quickly grasp it with forceps, or hold it between your fingernail and thumb, then cauterize its roots. If the forceps cannot take a grip of them because they are too moist, grab them with a piece of cloth, cotton wool or chamois leather, remove them with two fingers, then cauterise them, sprinkle some hot powder over them which acts as a cautery; you may also cauterise them according to what is written in the chapter on cauterization. You can use other treatments until it heals. If the anus cannot be extruded, then administer an irritating enema and harsh one so that they can wash away whatever is inside the rectum, which will allow the haemorrhoids to protrude clearly; once the patient has strained themselves, and the haemorrhoid has come out of the anus, then treatment is easy. This involves grasping them with fingernail or forceps, cauterising them as we have said, until it heals, being careful about incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: 
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	By drying out of faeces from the bowel/rectum.
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Often there is drying out of faeces in the intestine, due to constraint by natural forces and when illness is longstanding and does not respond to treatment.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	You should apply a thin layer of bark from a spathil or your nail to the area, preventing it from becoming moist; then treat until it is firm as required; if it cannot seal, repeat the shaving more vigorously than before until there is abundant healing and scarring; subsequently treat again once healed.
dou fremit	From swelling.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	A formix is a small faulty appearance between the body and goes very deep; sometimes it finds cold, and one feels it like death from swelling, and appears all over the body but most in hands rather than other places.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is such that you take a cane made from a goose quill, or a strong vulture feather, and place this cane on the trembling [part of the body], so that the purple circles touch the trembling all around; then turn your hand over the entire cane so that you grip all around the trembling, and put it in perfectly, and uproot the trembling from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see fit, make such a cane from copper or iron according to this form, and let it be thin below and thick above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not pierce it, to hold with your finger, and press it; And if you see fit, cauterize the trembling, as is described in the chapter on cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	Of the form of the clyster
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes the clyster is made of silver or tin, or melted and wrought brass; and sometimes these instruments are small and great, according to what they are adapted for.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those which we adapt for the treatment of children and those who are weak and full of pain are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the small and great clyster is thus broadly as follows: the bellies are tied according to this manner
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And it has a discharge where the bellies are tied, as you can see, and the head is pierced inside; and have on one side two perforations, and on the other one; and be the bellies in which one places medicines of a beast's bladder or parchment, and be pierced all around with small perforations, and have between each perforation one finger's breadth, then thrust into these perforations a strong thread of twisted silk wound in an X or round about, and assemble the belly as if it were a goatskin; and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument in front with a strong thread, then clysterize; and this is the form of the circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicament not be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the tube with oil or egg white, or similar substance, then gently insert it; then squeeze the minister's II hands together until it is entirely out, then remove the tube, and lift the patient's legs against the wall, and if the medicament wishes to come out, hold it in as much as you can; and if he sleeps a whole night through, so much the better.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you give him an enema for a bellyache, and the medicament comes out quickly, repeat it until he is cured.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if there are haemorrhoids at the anus or abscesses, then let the enema be as gentle as for a child; and this is the form of the subtle tube with its tight skin:
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have spoken of the treatment of wounds in the previous division; now we will discuss the art of healing and medicine according to its practice.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what has caused them, where they have been inflicted, and by which means.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	Wounds are caused by various things such as the impact of stones, sword cuts and other sharp objects, or blows from lances, sticks, arrows, or similar instruments; also depending on where they occur in the body, like wounds that fall upon the neck, head, foot, belly, liver, and similar parts. I shall explain to you the treatment for each wound, beginning with simple head injuries since remembrance will come in its own chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound occurs on the head, and the bone is not broken, take note if it is due to a stone impact or similar things, and the skin is still intact but the wound is large, and you mildly suspect an inflamed abscess: then cause the patient to bleed immediately with the cephalic vein especially if little blood comes from the wound, and let the bleeding be contrary to the injured part; and prevent the patient from overeating wine and fatty meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not wish to bleed, then let his food be reduced, and let him neither drink wine nor eat meat; and place on the wound, if inflamed abscesses occur, moist cotton in rose oil alone or in astringent wine; and if there is no hot abscess, then apply to the wound, while it is fresh with all its blood, and has not been moved by air, the powder which I will mention shortly; and if the air has moved it, then apply certain ointments until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	Et if the wound is large like that of a sword cut or similar, and the lips cannot be brought together with stitches, then bring them together by sewing, as I will explain for wounds in the belly, regarding suturing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to the bone, jagged, and holds only by a little piece of skin, cut it away; then treat the wound with medicine, restore hard flesh in place of leather, and instruct the patient to eat coarse meat, such as testicles and wheat porridge, as well as chicken, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find rotten flesh on the skin, but it has not reached the bone, then cut away all the rottenness and throw it out, then treat it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein from which blood does not cease, and it cannot be staunched with medicine, then tie off the artery, and if you find it severed, bind it with a thread; and if this brings no benefit, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: you should put this powder on it so that the art [of medicine] moves [cures] them.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	The manner of the powder is as follows: take one part frankincense; two parts dragon's blood [a red resin]; three parts quicklime [a white or pale grey fine powder], and finely grind this powder, then apply it to the wound, pressing it firmly until it dries well and joins with all its blood; then bind it tightly, leaving it unloosened, if there is no swelling; for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And at times one uses only lime [calcium oxide] when there is no frankincense or dragon's blood available, but the art has healed the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the fire has cauterized the wound, especially in summer, do not put this powder on it; instead, apply some digestive ointments or poultices made of barley flour with water and honey until it exudes pus; then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the bone fracture occurs with the wound, and it is minor, extract it with fine pincers; I will tell you later about skull fractures.
de la plaie dou col	of the neck wound.
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound occurs on the neck and it is straightforward, there is no distinction between this and a head injury; however, if the carotid artery or the jugular vein in the neck has been severed, this is critical.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the head, there is no other remedy but to leave it alone and put nothing constraining on it, as it harms the head and makes it retreat; and put nothing cold on the wound, because the substance of the head is cool, and its connection is with the brain, which is the highest organ; instead, use gentle medicine, such as balm washed in clean water, and mixed with rose oil, and cucumber also washed in clean water, and other stones depending on this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, cut it and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and full of filth, open it further down to where it is deeper; and if the artery is cut, and blood flows from it, open it, clean it, and cauterize if necessary; and if the spine of the neck is cut or the heart and its ducts are affected so that breathing is possible, then sever the heart above the neck vertebrae, without touching the neck but resetting it according to its natural shape; then bind it carefully, leaving it untouched for a few days, after which treat it with drying ointments until it is healed; and if the wound has compressed into bone, clean it; and if there are pieces of bone, bring those you can together strongly, and leave those that cannot be brought close to decay, let the wound suppurate, and alleviate any discharge; and if the wound is fresh, apply a powder over the powder I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound with a fistula, treat it as I have described in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	Of the wound from a lance or knife.
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a lance or knife wound, and the injury is deep, look to see if there are signs of wind escaping when the patient breathes: know then that the wound is deadly. If it is not deep, and fresh with all its blood, do not apply powder nor bandage it for the blood should not be stopped from flowing freely back to the heart, which would kill the patient; instead apply an attractive ointment, and dress it twice a day. If you have no ointment, put old cotton in the wound to absorb fluids, and let the patient sleep on their injury for three days or four or more: there will be no spasm nor bad tremors of the heart nor strange breathings; and when you see these good signs, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure it then with dressings and other treatments until it is healed; if it cannot be healed, operate as you see fit to treat the fistula; apply the appropriate treatment.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	If the wound is an incision from a sword or knife, and it is simple, on the arm or back, treat what is visible first; if it is large, use sutures; if small, apply powder; if it has penetrated the bone, breaking pieces, clean the wound, realigning any displaced tissue; if it is not dislocated, let the wound fester and ease extractions; other wounds to other limbs are judged as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	Rupture of the abdomen
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The rupturing of the belly occurs in many ways: great and small; from a large wound sometimes the intestines or the nerves of the intestines may emerge, causing hernia; and suturing is more difficult, and often the smaller wound causes greater harm than the larger one, for it is harder to replace the intestines, unless they are replaced immediately. Because the intestine swells quickly when it feels the cold, so they retreat even more tightly, hence the small wound is preferable, because the intestine can be placed back in its place easier than others. And know that there are four kinds of abdominal rupture: the two ordinary suturing techniques occur in the abdomen and the suturing of other bodily wounds; while two other specific types of sutures are common to other wounds, although they are more appropriate for the abdomen wound, and I will speak about each one individually and explain it.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and something from the intestine has come out, and it is a difficult thing to replace, this can be done in one of two ways: either due to the small size of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner: moisten a sponge or soft cloth in lukewarm water only, or cook it in water with vinegar and cypress and spike, and apply to the intestine until the swelling is reduced; and sometimes do this with restraining wine, which helps to reduce the inflammation.
