Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling subside, moisten the intestine with water or cook elderberries and mallow, as these alleviate any further enlargement; and if nothing can enter, make a small incision in the wound with the instrument used to cut hemorrhoids; and the first treatment is advisable for the opening, so that one should not enlarge it without great necessity; here are the instruments to use: make an incision on the inside of the curve and outwards, and see this form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines have come out, then replace them carefully according to their natural form into their proper place, if you are able, for this is better.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is in the lower part of the abdomen, you should make the patient lie on their back, with their legs elevated above their head; and if it is in the upper part of the abdomen, place the head and chest higher than the lower parts; also, if the abdominal rupture is in one of the two halves, focus your attention on ensuring that the injured part is positioned higher than the other; thus, you must manage as I say for large and medium-sized wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, use what is available to you, then have someone with gentle hands assist by holding the entire rupture in their hand and bringing together its lips; this is a common method of suturing, involving taking either one or multiple needles according to the size of the wound's width, leaving a finger-length space at its head before threading it with a good strong thread; pierce both sides of the skin with two ends of catgut that lies beneath, until you make them emerge from that part and bring together the four ends in pairs; then draw a double thread around the needle from either side, bringing together the lips of the wound neatly, leaving another finger-length space before inserting another needle; tie the thread as for the first one, repeating this according to need with any number of needles until the entire wound is sutured, using medium-sized needles (not too fine or they'll cut through all the tissue but not so thick that they won't fit); be careful not to pierce beyond the flesh and skin, lest you tear open the wound before it has a chance to heal; then clip off the ends of the needle so as not to prick the patient while sleeping, and place lint or cloth around these points to hold them in place until the wound is healed. This method of suturing with needles is more suitable for small wounds because only one or two are needed. The second type of suture is common: you bring together both sides of the skin and catgut ends into a single medium-sized needle, threaded with strong thread; after piercing all four lips together, draw the needle back to where it began in the manner of sewing cloth, leaving the thickness of one finger between each stitch. This method I used on a man whose abdomen was torn open by knife, the wound over a palm wide and intestines protruding two palms out, the wound itself being mid-belly
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned his intestine after it had been outside for twenty-four hours, and the wound was healed up to fifteen days, I treated him, and he was cured.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the doctors had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; I did not treat him with ointments because I was in a place where they were not found, nor any medicines; instead, I applied old cotton twice a day on the wound, and washed it with honey water until he healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of suturing: take the needle and pass it from outside to inside; when it has pierced through directly, leave the chief end of the siphon or gut where you inserted the needle, and make it pierce from the other side, from inside to out; this type of suture is done in such a way that you sew as furriers do with skins, leaving one edge of the wound and then taking it up again on the other side until the whole suture is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of stitching, as Galen properly describes it, is like this: some do it by naturally bringing the two parts together and applying one head of the wound to the other, in such a way: insert a needle into one head of the spleen close by, and pierce that place alone, leaving the two heads of the pancreas; then turn the needle, and pierce through from the outside part to the inside, at the two heads of the spleen; then pierce each of them from the outside part to the inside, in the other two heads of the spleen which are on the opposite side; and this is the most common type of stitching.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen says this word, and some testify that one should stitch the belly with two needles, each having a thread; and you must push one needle from one side, and the other from the opposite side, in the manner of those who sew belts; and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly, the stitching is more grievous than in other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgements of the wound are such as those of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, rather than let it be moved by fire, keep the intestine cool, and treat the wound; then apply a powder made from charred flesh, and if it has been moved by fire, use an ointment that is at hand, until the wound heals; and stitch the skin, and ensure the sinews are joined, and the tendons; then treat the wound like any other, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, apply old cotton immediately as it begins to heal, moving it twice a day until it is cured.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you will not need any other medicine in various situations when the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound might become infected with the principal limbs, then it is necessary to moisten light woollen cloth with oil of a moderate temperature or rose oil, and apply this around the affected areas and under the armpits; and if there is pain or swelling in the belly, which happens often, cleanse it with diluted red wine, especially if the infection has reached the intestine; pierce it inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine which is called 'jeun' cannot be healed when it is wounded, and this is due to the fragility of its veins, and because of the delicacy of the whole body, and the proximity of its nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the serous membrane springs out of the wound, put it back in as with the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and has turned greenish or black, then you must bind the place that is black so no blood flows from it, for there are veins and arteries; then cut away what lies between the binding, and tie both ends of this to the part below the wound until outside to ease the extraction when the serous membrane falls, and the wound bows.
de la routure dou boueil	On the rupture of the mouth
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is perforated and the wound is small, it can be restored in some cases, for I have seen a man pierced in the belly by a lance; and the wound was to the right of the stomach, and became inflamed and turned into a fistula, from which issued egestion and flatulence; I treated him as best I could, and did not cease until he was healed, and his flesh knit together.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him healed, I feared the patient might still have pain in his belly; and there was no pain, but he remained in better condition, eating and drinking; and some experts said that for a small wound in the intestine, it must be bound thus: take two large-headed wooden pegs, then bring together the lips of the wound, and when the peg has opened its mouth, place it on both lips so that it holds them tightly shut; then cut off one head of the peg, and leave it so that it cannot come undone, then insert another peg in the same way as before, until the whole wound is secured; then dress the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine,
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it heals, is universally called a "fistula", especially when it is healed and bowed inwards.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And fistula is truly a faulty hard and white nodule, where there is no pain, and it is also bowed like the feather of a bird; sometimes it jumps outwards and at other times inwards, sometimes small and often large enough, and I have already spoken about this in the section on wounds, that any wound which has not healed and lacks flesh, is always caused by one of nine reasons: either due to the deficiency of blood or pus; or its malignancy; or because it contains hard matter within and around its lips, preventing new flesh from growing; or there is too much pus; or the wound is poisoned and the matter is of poor quality; or the medicine for treating it is inadequate; or due to corruption by some manner of pestilence; or because the region's nature has a delayed digestion, slow healing, and swelling; or if there are veins or bones involved: I have already shown all these causes, their signs, and appropriate treatments.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now I must inform you of the treatment for fistula, which is performed by manual operation.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that fistula can occur in any part of the body; for there are fistulas which come to large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the anus, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to some ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and such that comes to the principal part of a member, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	All the fistulas that are of this nature are difficult to treat and heal, and there is only hard work and ignorance involved; if there is any fistula which does not reach the place I mentioned, and you have faith in its cure, and you can identify it, then take a probe made of brass or iron, if the fistula is straight, so seek it out; but if the fistula is twisted, use a thin brass probe, for brass bends to fit into twists; and if there are many openings to the fistula, and you cannot thoroughly examine them with probes, then wash it out through one of these openings, as moisture will pass from one opening to another, washing it clean; thereafter examine it carefully by probing until you know whether there is bone or nerve present, and whether it ends cleanly, ask the patient about any pain they feel when you press your hand upon their body, and where exactly this feeling arises; once you are certain of its true location, and how close to a joint, or nerve, artery or vein, or in one of the places I mentioned before, then proceed as follows: cut into it according to what I have said, remove scabs and rotten flesh that is inside; thereafter treat until healed, and if this fistula is deep and straight, you must carefully cut out all matter until there remains nothing except healthy tissue, then insert probes moistened in caustic medicine right up to the head of the fistula, so that the superfluous waste at its base might be eaten away by the corrosive properties of the medicine; thereafter apply ointments which encourage healing of healthy flesh until it is completely healed. If this does not work, cauterize as mentioned before and if bone has been affected by the fistula then you must cut out the bone.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If neither the bone nor flesh burden your main limbs, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, with putrefaction and blackening present, let it reign until all corruption is removed, then treat subsequent matters by cutting away flesh until it is healed; and if it isn't healed and returns bowed like before, know that you haven't reached bottom: so uncover and seek until you reach the base, and remove all corruption, then restore its place; and if it thus heals, well done.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach; there are other natural agents for this situation; and if there's a small corrupted bone, which you can extract with pincers, remove it using an appropriate instrument; and if multiple bones are present, extract them all at once, leaving none behind; and if moisture causes opposition, without error or fear, cut through both moisture and flesh to deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, apply something that causes putrefaction to the wound, and leave it until the flesh is rotten around the bone, and then they will more easily extract the bones; and if it is a large bone, like in the leg or thigh, scrape away only the corruption until all blackness is gone, then restore the wound; and if a great part of the putrefied matter has extended to the marrow of the bone, you must treat it by cutting out all that is corrupt down to the marrow, then cure it so that it heals completely; I will tell you about a fistula which happened in a man's leg, from which you can take an example and aid your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was this young man around thirty years old who had pain in his leg due to an internal cause, such that the matter came out into the leg and became swollen with a large abscess which did not have any external reason for opening; but through their foolishness the surgeons worked on it until they opened up the abscesses, and much matter flowed from them, then it turned into a fistula, and many holes formed, all of which emitted foul and moist matter from his body; many surgeons had treated him with cures over two years without any wise man in the art of medicine, so I was called to see him, and saw his leg as well as the medicines they were treating him with, and that which came out through the holes in great quantity; the young man's flesh became red where these matters issued from, and had a yellow colour.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I set up a tent in one of these holes, and then examined all the holes, and found that one came against the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I hurried and cut into one of the holes until I exposed a part of the bone, and found it corrupted and perforated, with the corruption reaching deep inside; I cleaned what appeared to be the corrupted bone, believing there was no other corruption beyond what I removed; and so I began to restore the wound with soothing medicines for a long time, but it would not heal; then I started again, exposing the bone as before, and found that the corruption had continued into the bone, so I cleaned it and then removed it, trying to close the site; but I could not, even when I cut around an inch of the bone, which was all soft tissue, before restoring it with medicines; and it healed swiftly, without need for further treatment beyond the patient's weakness, who could not endure more, and my fear of death from him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the evacuation, he often bled, but he was completely healed, and in place of the bone, a hard tissue grew, and it had good consistency and caused no harm or damage whatsoever, neither going nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	If the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be treated like this: take a linen cloth and pull it over the exposed end of the bone, and ask someone to stretch it upwards; then place another larger piece of cloth on top of the flesh covering the bone, stretching the head [of the bone], so that you push away the corrupted tissue underneath, and uncover the area where you want to operate, being careful not to cut into healthy flesh; next, put a red-hot iron or an iron rod under the bone in order to cauterize the corrupted tissue; make sure to remove all traces of corruption when operating, then do it again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupt and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, uncover all the flesh; then place a hot iron underneath, and with the iron move from one side to the other over the corruption, let it be so long as our described; and if the corruption is in the joint, cut out the corrupt joint, and clean the bone on either side of this; and if the corruption continues through two joints, there is nothing else for it but to cut; and if the corruption is at the wrist of the hand or ankle of the foot, that place is very strong, yet you must search into the nature of that corrosion, how it reveals itself to you; and cleanse it in every way possible, without harming the sinews or nerves. Know that there are many cutting instruments for bones according to their position, appearance, size, subtlety, large or small dimensions, hardness etc.; therefore it is necessary to match each kind of instrument with a different work required; know also that the work shows you what instrument you need by the knowledge and skill in this art, and from observation of the symptoms shown in sicknesses. Therefore think about the tools needed for your operation as described above.
dou feu	Of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The head putrefies either internally or externally; and when you have treated that decay by the cure of medicines, and it does not benefit, then you must amputate that limb up to the place where the decay originates, so that the patient escapes death, or the greater evil, which is the defect of the member itself; and here's a sign: the member becomes black, as if burned in fire, and after the blackness, the decay spreads from one member to another, taking over the entire body. So you must hasten amputation before it comes down to that, and if this corrosion was caused by the sting of venomous creatures like scorpions or snakes, cut off at the top part of the thumb, do not give any space for it to reach all the way up to the hand itself
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	Et si décorruption du sang vient quant tu ouvres, si cautérise le lieu aussitôt, ou tu mets sur certaines poudres rétrécissantes; puis reviens à ta médecine tant qu'elle est accomplie, puis lie le membre nu d'un lien convenable, et soigne-le jusqu'à ce qu'il soit cicatrisé; et je te raconterai qu'il arriva à un homme en son pied: il lui arriva une noirceur qui semblait être une brûlure de feu, et cette corrosion vint premièrement sur son doigt du pied, jusqu'à ce qu'elle couvre tout le pied; et quand l'homme vit la corrosion, il se hâta de couper le pied, et fut guéri; et longtemps après, la corrosion revint sur le doigt de sa main, et il vint me voir, et je lui mis des choses répercussives après avoir nettoyé son corps, mais les corrosions ne purent cesser; et il comprit que je devais lui couper la main, et je n'en voulus rien faire, car j'avais l'espoir de soigner le mal; et j'eus aussi peur qu'il meure si je taillais sa main, car ses forces étaient faibles; et il désespéra tout, et retourna dans son pays, et se hâta de se couper la main, et fut guéri; et je n'ai pas pu raconter plus que pour ce qui doit être fait autrement, s'il en a besoin.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Sometimes an abscess arises in fleshy places and persists for so long that it forms a large accumulation of pus; then it ruptures and pierces the skin like a pot, leaving the place bare just as if it were a vessel; the skin which is above is as delicate as thin cloth and does not extend down to the bone or nerve. Such diseases are called "sinus" and not "fistula"; but when they reach all the way through the bone into the marrow then they are called "fistula", and the skin around it should be cut away, especially if it is delicate like a cloth; one does not fear its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you are concerned that the skin may corrupt and the corruption is not deep but there is some flesh around it, then treat it with an enema in this way: first see if the sinus is large or small; whether its contents have a foul odor and are coming from deeper down within. Then make your enema out of Egyptian medicine which you will prepare as follows: take equal amounts of verdigris, oil, and litharge put them into a vessel over heat until it becomes red and thick like honey. Take what is necessary according to the size of the sinus add water and honey; with this enema you can clean out any remaining pus by squeezing the orifice shut for two hours after inserting the medicine then letting it come out freely afterwards. If sometimes these medicines are not available one may use ashes instead mixed into water when they become like a paste which is also helpful in cleaning out sinuses that have been made dirty by other things such as Egyptian ointments etc.; but if neither can be tolerated add some honey mixed with wine since this has the property of cleansing while still keeping everything clean at all times; and afterwards apply emollients to help new tissue form again - either use diaphanite plaster which you will prepare beforehand using rose oil mixed into red wine or else simply apply one of many other ointments mentioned previously depending on what is available there. If however the aperture leading down into where pus has accumulated happens to be small and cannot easily accommodate an enema tube then stretch it out slightly with a thin iron rod first before applying some type Egyptian ointment such basilicon within so that space becomes wider accordingly; but should opening happen instead due either cutting off too much tissue surrounding wound area (thus creating larger than needed hole) simply leave behind only single layer covering entire wound surface while removing anything extra below.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the bowels are in their natural state, they do not allow meat to be digested; and if you cannot cut open the breast as you wish, then arrange it so that the bowel moves down to its lowest point, for when the bowels are healthy, they do not allow meat to be digested. And if you cannot cut open the breast in the manner you want, prepare them in such a way: let the bowel descend gently and leave nothing of the bowel behind; take consolidating medicines to place on the wound, and stretch over it a linen cloth that covers the entire wound; then cut with force at the right spot where the breast is a little wider than the first incision, stretching the ointment onto another piece of fabric according to the amount needed for the wound. Place this fabric onto the breast wound in order to ease the bowel movement and do not remove the large cloth that covers it until after many days have passed once; and remove the one placed on top of the breast often to relieve the bowels, and clean off whatever is coming out from them, whether it be poison or a little or enough, digested or undigested. Take note if the patient feels pain or not, and whether there are abscesses present in addition to this; once your medicine has been applied as described above, you will know that the wound has already healed when you see nature emerge from the breast incision. Then approach the saints and afterwards release the bowels every morning for three days while changing their cloth each time and renewing its ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast ejects undigested food after many days, know that the breast is not healthy.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle venom emerges after a long time, do not despair of health, for healing is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are people whose wounds take a long time to heal, and others who do the opposite; if undigested food comes out of the breast after many days, know that the breast is not healing; and if the breast takes too long to heal, and it becomes prolonged, you should apply drying medicines that are moist in substance but dry in nature, such as a fine ointment, for there is a great deal of vitriol in it, which is the last medicine used. Take this fine ointment, made with rose oil, and moisten it with an equal amount of old wine; then smear it on and use it. This same treatment works better when cooked and thickened if the aforementioned fine ointments are not available. Use myrrh, aloes, and incense instead, grind them together, add powder to honey while still over the fire, mix well and apply onto a piece of cloth. Place the cloth over the breast and administer for some time; you may use aristologus longa (a type of herb) or roots from lilium candidum (or its flour-like powder), centaury (centaureae herba). Use either single herbs or mixtures, grind them up into a powder and mix with honey as I said before. If the cure is prolonged and does not heal even after this treatment then know that corruption has reached deeper layers of tissues and bone, causing hard masses in soft tissue; treat it like an abscess fistula (a type of skin infection), as we have described earlier.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	Of an abscess under the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess that forms beneath the nail of the thumb, or toe, or occasionally elsewhere; and when it becomes old, and no attention is paid to it, it develops into a deep-seated abscess, discharging pus until it erodes the root of the nail, and sometimes even destroys it entirely; then there is bone exposure, causing stench and swelling, and the digit becomes broad, with an ugly color.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the previous section, and the treatment is not effective, then it is necessary to cut away all the remaining unhealthy tissue near the nail with an iron tool, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cauterizations are a great help if the bone is healthy and the nail is sound; and if the nail presses on the flesh, starts to prick, and wounds it, then you must place a slender rod under the nail that pricks the flesh, pushing it upwards, and cut away this flesh carefully and lightly, applying caustic and corrosive medicines to remove all of it; then treat with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	If the corrosion is in the bone, cut it away and treat with boiling oil, for as long as there is corrupted bone, it cannot heal; and if you see the finger becoming corrupt, then cut it off close to the hand as described above, then treat until it is healed; and if it is wounded and pierced, and feels great pain, then you must first cleanse it; then cut the nail with a sharp spatula by cutting across it, making sure the incision does not reach the flesh beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and should this happen, apply something to ease the pain.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of the shoulder joint from the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two adjusting thumbs that are born in some people's hands are sometimes very fleshy, and there is either skin or bones; at times they have nails, and one of them grows on the root of the joint, while the birth occurs in several of us.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	One that is born in the root of the thumb does not move, and one that is born on the joint of the thumb sometimes moves; the size of the fleshy one should be cut at its root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	One that is born in the root of the joint is difficult to treat: make sure you take care of it.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In one who is born or must be delivered by the posterior route, you must first cut the round flesh down to the bone, then cut the bone to a suitable depth for it, and cure it until it heals.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The joining together of bones occurs either by birth, or by the healing of a wound, or by burning with fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	You should cut this fusion so that the bones can repair according to their natural shapes; then place between them two tents or oiled wet cloths, so they do not fuse together; or you can put between them two pieces of fine lead, until the joints are healed as they should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If a fusion occurs on someone's hand with the palm facing upwards, cut this fusion as it is required.
des vils	des villages
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Worms are large veins wrapped in excess melancholy humours that come from many parts of the body; and they occur more often in the legs of those who walk on foot and work, carrying loads, than others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	So it is necessary for you to administer purging of the bile sometimes, then treat with the basil plant.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment with iron is done in two ways: one is by cauterizing and drawing out the black blood; and the other way is that you lift the vein and draw all of it out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The cut is done in this way: first immerse the leg in very hot water until the large blood vessels are softened, then stretch the patient's leg from above the thigh to below the knee; then make an incision on one spot or two or three spots, a wide one, and lift it up and draw out the black blood with your hand, from one end to the other, as long as there is still enough blood coming for the patient to withstand; and then bind it up, and command that he abstains from eating meat which produces black bile; and repeat the evacuation and treatment when the veins are full again, if it harms the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The treatments for the wound are as follows: remove the patient's leg hair if there is any, then place it in a bath, and bathe the leg with hot water until it turns red and the veins swell; and if you have no bath, heat it over fire, and then scrape along the vein from long to knee or ankle joint; then cut open the skin with an instrument, and peel back the skin on either side of the vein until it appears when felt underneath; and one can see it as red and black, appearing like a white cord when looked at under the skin; then push a thread beneath it, lifting it away from the skin, then cut lightly in another spot three inches above; then peel back the skin over the vein once more until it is exposed, then lift it with the thread as before, and cut again at an other location one inch above; then make several more cuts if necessary, then lift it up, and make a final cut at the patient's toe bone, pulling and lifting until you reach the second incision made earlier; remove it by incision after incision until all is out, then cut off any remaining ends; and should you be unable to pull or lift it, thread a needle with strong double thread and tie it on, then draw it through, turning your hand from side to side as it comes out; be careful not to cut the vein, for if one does so, it cannot be pulled nor lifted and would harm the patient further; once you have extracted all of it, place soaked wool in wine and rose oil onto the wound site; treat until healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the face is contorted and twisted and rolled together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must split it crookedly, but do not cut it; and draw it as we have mentioned before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron with which one cuts the face is curved, and does not slice, so as not to cut the vein; and it has a thick curve, for if it were thin, it would cut the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and here is its shape:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is engendered in the legs, in warm parts where grass or trees do not grow, and on land that has no moisture; and perhaps it grows elsewhere other than in the legs, and this occurs due to putrefaction that arises from under the skin, just as serpents and worms arise within the body, bred between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the sign of the beginning of this vein is that a great inflammation comes to the leg, then the color changes, and the vein starts to protrude, just like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the vein opens, you must wrap around a piece of lead that is 3 and a half to 2 inches long, tie it up, and let the lead hang on the leg. Whenever some part of it protrudes, wrap the lead again and retie it; if it is too long, cut off a portion and rewrap the rest but do not cut at its root until all of it has been removed; because if you cut it, it will retract into the flesh, causing an abscess and putrefaction in that spot, as well as a bad disease. So one must treat this vein little by little up to its head without leaving any part inside; often when this vein is treated it may be 5 palms or 10 long, there was once a man who came to me with such a vein issuing from his leg for 10 palms in length and after cutting into it one root or channel issued forth, then perforate the whole thing so that all of it issues out; empty the material within, and apply healing medicines against putrefaction every day, then treat like abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes this vein is more delicate, especially when it appears in the ankle joint, or where the foot joins, and there are many perforations, making it fragile; treat it then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Worms that are born between the skin and flesh.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called "ox disease" in our land because it often occurs in cattle, and it is a small worm that is born between the skin and flesh, moving throughout the body up and down, and one can feel its movement from limb to limb, until it tears open the skin where it was, and falls out; it is caused by the decay of certain humors, just as worms, serpents, and lumbricals come from the belly; we doubt its maliciousness because when it moves through the body and reaches the head, sometimes entering the eye, and destroying it. This happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it curing and spreading, one cannot escape except when it goes: therefore, you must tightly bind the place above and below with a strong bond, then cut above and pull out the core, and if the poison is deeply embedded in the flesh, and you do not find it, cauterize it with fire until it dies; and the greatest harm that it does, is to run into the eye, as we have said; and if you see it approaching the head near the eye, strongly constrict the eyebrow below it, then cut above, and pull out the core; and the patient must use bodily cleansing medicines of solutive medicines for bad, rotten humors, and avoid consuming foods that cause decay.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from windiness.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that appears in certain limbs, and can move from limb to limb; and I saw what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to see a sick woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and soon after, it appeared like a worm rising towards the shoulder, more than anything else, like quicksilver when it flows from one place to another; the pain left that spot, settled into the shoulder, and then shortly afterwards spread throughout the body, until it reached the other arm; she then told me that it kept circling around her body, just as I had seen.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how it moved from limb to limb, because I had never before seen this illness behave in such a manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Toutevoie, I avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, but I ne l’avoie mie wants, si com je le vis en la femme; and I me pensai that c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste reason a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, and li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, and puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; and cauterize le leu; and se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, and pilules de serapin, and semblans autres.
des saiettes	from arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and the parts of the body where they land.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of arrows is such that there are those with large points, small ones, barbed, and solid; there are also those with two angles, some with long shafts, and others composed of several pieces; moreover, an arrow can penetrate a limb in one of two ways: it may strike a vital organ like the brain, heart, liver, lungs, kidneys, intestines, bladder or similar organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When an arrow strikes any of these organs and the sign of death appears, which I will tell you about later, then it is necessary to be wary of extracting this arrow because many die afterward in different circumstances; when this evil sign does not appear and the arrow is not deeply embedded, draw it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when an arrow falls and pierces the bone, and breaks the thin layer that is above the brain, it is when your sight becomes dark and dim, and you see green and red in one eye, and there is inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and confusion of the mind, and vomiting bile; and perhaps blood flows from the nostrils or ears without cause; and maybe they lose speech and voice; and also white moist matter oozes out of the wound, resembling pus, and also like burnt flesh; if these signs appear to you, stay away from treatment, and remove the arrow if it remains there.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the arrow when it falls on the heart are that it is near the left breast, and they also feel as if it were stuck in a hard object, not empty; and perhaps the pulse changes like an arrow, and black blood flows out, and coldness and cold sweat appear, and fainting: know then without doubt that death is descending.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrowhead that has not pierced the lung is that there is no foam coming out of the wound, and the throat swells up, and the patient's complexion changes, and they breathe heavily while rejecting cold drinks.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrowhead falls into the lining of the lung, it is near the small ribs; it causes great pain and difficulty breathing along with heavy sighing; and it affects all the limbs from the shoulders downwards.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrowhead falls into the stomach, sometimes something undigested may come out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrowhead falls into the belly, and no excrement comes out through the lower intestine, there is no hope for a cure or the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine jumps out and flows forth, and the patient feels intense pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, such as the arm and forearm, neck, throat, shoulder, armpit, backbone, waist, thigh, legs, and similar parts are safe according to many arrangements.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or an artery and it is not poisoned, as I will tell you happened to me so that you can do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man that an arrow fell on his cheekbone into the root of his nose: I grasped it and pulled it from underneath through the ear's fat, and he was cured without incident.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And drive an arrow into a wound so that it ends up in the fat beneath the eyelid, and the arrow is blunt, and one can only reach its tip towards the shaft, and this arrow was as large as a Turkish bow, all of iron but light without barbs; the wound was cauterized, and no ill befell him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And I drew an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and this arrow was Arabian with barbs; I cut away the flesh, and manipulated it until I extracted it, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And I drew an arrow from a man, which was embedded in his belly, and I thought he would die; after thirty days had passed, there was no change in his condition; so I incised the skin over the arrow, manipulated it, and extracted it, and he suffered no ill effects.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you have a man with an arrow lodged in his back or shoulder, and the wound has healed over it; yet the arrow remains within him, and it hasn't changed its natural position nor caused any harm to his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And consider another man with an arrow lodged in his face, and the wound has healed over it; remaining thus without causing him great pain or other significant distress.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And treat an arrow wound in the prince's servant, where the arrow had penetrated his nose and was slightly inclined towards the right side; the arrow itself was entirely bent. I was called to perform the cure after it had been there for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found that the wound was quite narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I sought it everywhere with a subtle touch, yet felt naught; he sensed pricking and pain beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the tip of the arrowhead I applied a drawing and digestive poultice there so that the flesh would not swell; and the flesh above the arrowhead became apparent.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I left the poultice on longer, and the wound healed initially, but the patient remained ill for a long time, feeling the arrowhead inside his nose every day; he told me so himself.
