Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied a corrosive medicine to the wound for many days until it opened up, and I probed it, feeling the arrowhead's tip moving in place; then I adjusted the medicine inside the wound's opening so that the arrowhead's head became clearly visible; after four months of waiting, the arrowhead finally moved enough for me to widen the wound with forceps, which I inserted from one side and another but could not extract it; so I kept devising and ingeniously crafting instruments until one day I seized the arrowhead with properly-made forceps as described in this chapter's end, pulling it out and closing the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the surgeons judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored; so I restored it then, and the wound was healed, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or I have told you about the quality of extracting certain arrows, so that you focus your attention on what I do not say, for books cannot cover everything; but wise masters compare many great things, and for what is present and lacking, find new work, and new instruments, in the treatment of strange cases which occur in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows exit the body in which they are embedded either through the way they entered or from another part; and those that must come out through where they went in are arrows lodged in soft tissue, and this may occur at any time.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not jump now, leave it until the flesh is rotten around [the arrow], and the exit point is loosened; and also if it is stuck in the bone, and cannot come out, then let it remain for a few days, moving it each day; and then it will jump, and if it does not, then pierce all around with a very fine saw until the surrounding bone is widened, and then pull [the arrow] out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head and goes up to one of the membranes of the brain, and any of the accidents I have mentioned appear in the patient: do not pull it out, but leave it until it is even after a few days, because if the arrow reaches the surface, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not stuck solely in bone, and does not emerge from the skin, and the patient remains without incident for a few days, prepare to extract it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply embedded like this and cannot exit through the skin, apply tourniquets around as I told you; then treat the wound until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is lodged within the body where it cannot be seen, search for it throughout; and if you can feel it, extract it with a suitable instrument; and if due to the tightness of the wound, or the depth of the arrow, there are no bones, nerves or veins involved, make an incision until the wound is large enough; draw out the arrow if possible, and if it has barbs that hold it in place, remove flesh stuck on two sides as much as you can, then break or bend the barbs so you may withdraw it; do this carefully lest you snap the arrow which would make extraction more difficult.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, leave it until the surrounding flesh is rotten; then pull it out, as the extraction would be eased.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the loss of blood makes you hesitate, so manage what we have said about treatment in its chapter; and beware of cutting into a nerve or opening a vein, instead use devices to draw out the arrow without danger, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; place the patient according to how they were when the arrow struck them, for this is the greatest aid available, and if you cannot, then lay him as the signs show.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	If the arrow comes from another place, or nothing appears of it, but the skin is swollen where it may be; cut open that spot until forceps can grip it and pull it out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is stuck in the bone, turn your hand roundly until it enters the bone and widens it, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	If it cannot come out, leave it be for now and then restart the extraction process until it finally exits; if there is an arrow shaft present, push on the entire shaft; and if it was blunt, and you want to administer a thrusting motion, use an instrument with a pointed end so that the tip of the arrow enters the aperture of the instrument; then give a final strong push, and if the arrowhead is stuck, insert the instrument with its point facing inwards to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is envenomed, you must cut away all flesh around it, if possible, and then treat the wound as necessary.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow falls onto the foot or belly or bladder or ribs, and it is close to the surface, and you can cut above it, then do so; be careful not to cut into the vein or nerve, then extract [the arrow], and then suture the wound if necessary; heal until it is whole.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the pliers used to extract arrows resembles the beak of a bird; see below for its form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many types of these pliers: large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the pointed end is also like a bird's feather, to push against the tip of the arrow, as shown here:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of the forceps for pushing and extracting is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	Common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	Of the veins from which one bleeds there are thirty-one, of which sixteen are in the head: two are the beating ones that lie behind the ears and are called 'herbech'; the two arteries that appear in the temples; the two veins lying at the corners of both eyes, which are called 'aspires', as well as a vein in the middle of the forehead; a vein in the centre of the head near the nose; two small veins that lie on either side of the neck; and finally two veins that are situated just above the mouth between the lips: these last ones being known as 'augeherich'; besides, there are also two veins below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins that are commonly treated for healing are five in each arm: one is the cephalic vein, which is located on the left side and known by laypeople as the "head vein"; the median vein is called the "fast" vein and composed of the cephalic and basilic; the latter is referred to as the "heart vein" by laypeople. The basilic lies on the right side and is called the "belly vein" by laymen, being located above the axillary artery; this is the vein used for healing, which becomes clearly visible in the armpit.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the superficial vein is located between the little finger and ring finger, having two branches; in the leg and foot there are three veins: one runs below the bend of the armpit on the left side, another passes through the right ankle; a third, known as the "nest" vein arises from the other ankle. In the opposite leg there are three veins that correspond to these.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The bleeding of the veins that are located behind the ears helps with chronic colds and headaches; and regarding the quality of the bleeding, as I told you, it is necessary to raise the patient's head, and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then, hold the patient's neck with a vise so that the two veins appear behind the ears in two dependent places from the head: look for them with your finger, and where you feel the pulse beneath your finger, make an incision there; then take the lancet, and insert it under the vein until reaching the bone, then lift your hand to open all the vein upwards, and cut both the skin and the vein well across two fingers wide, and let out blood as much as you want; then release and tie it up so that it is sealed; and I have already mentioned incision and cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The bleeding of the two arteries located in the temples is beneficial for treating chronic migraines, solid obstructions, and accustomed ophthalmitis, as well as acute lachrymal discharge from the eyes; and here are the characteristics of this treatment: the patient must extend their neck so that the two veins appear clearly; you should feel the pulse beneath your finger, then proceed to open up a vein below with a lancet; lift the heart upwards onto the vein using your index finger and insert the lancet underneath, lifting the vein as before when dealing with the other veins, and let blood flow according to your needs; release the patient and place your finger on top of the opened vein for an hour afterwards, then cover it in cotton; bind this firmly and leave until healed.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The bleeding of the vein in the forehead is equally effective as the bleeding of the temporal artery for ancient facial diseases, and for migraines, and for redness; its quality being that the patient twists their neck so much that the vein appears; then take the instrument which is called a "fosseur," whose form is this:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Place the tip on the vein and press it against your hand or another object, and allow blood to flow out according to the quantity you desire; then untie the patient's collar and bind the wound until it is healed, sometimes using a wide strip of cloth.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, the cloth strips should not be too sharp or pointed, and take care to bleed across the grain as the bone is nearby, for fear of breaking the strip when it is thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The bleeding of the two veins that are in the two temples aids the eyes, and [helps with] scabies, redness, inflammation in the eye, and diseases of the face; the quality of this bleeding is such that the patient tightens their neck by twisting with some cord, as before; then bleed them, and let the bleeding be crosswise, a little above the length of the flame and slightly wide, for there is no flesh [there].
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the veins are delicate, by chance they may break; then make the blood flow until you have what you need, and then bind it with cotton, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The bleeding of the vein in the nose is beneficial for fever, severe headache, and facial diseases, such as migraine and redness that appears on the face, especially when it is long-lasting; and the quality of this bleeding is such that the patient tightens their neck, then pulls their nose with your left hand, take the delicate, long vein, and insert it into the lip in the space between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open well downwards, and the blood will now begin to flow; do not go too far inside, and make the blood flow according to your need, then bind it for one night, as it heals quickly; this is the form of the vein:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The bleeding of the two jugular veins aids in relieving constriction of the throat, and at the onset of apoplexy, and in many illnesses, such as pleurisy, catarrh, herpes, and abscesses; and the quality of this treatment is that the patient must compress his neck with both hands, as we have said; and let the master stand above the head of the patient, and let the patient sit on a chair, then open the wound about an inch wide in length, then drain some blood gradually, or as much as necessary; then repeat this procedure for the other vein, then unfasten the binding, but tighten them slightly around all wounds so that they do not strangle the patient; and let him rest until morning, until the wounds are healed.
de la sainie des leivres	The bleeding of the lips
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The draining of veins from above helps with glue in the mouth, and gum corruption, and lip cracks, and from the nose and around it.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	Place the patient before you and restrict his neck as I said; then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one is on the right lip and the other on the left, and they are known by being black, and by the small black veins around them: so cut both of them, and if you do not know or are unsure which to take, just cut the thicker one from each side, and do this also for the two that lie above and below, because it is the same procedure.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	On bleeding beneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The bleeding of veins beneath the tongue is aided after the bleeding of the cephalic vein, and it is done at the narrowing of the throat, for diseases of the uvula, and ailments of the mouth; and the quality of the bleeder is such that the patient sits between your hands facing the sun, you lift their tongue, and look beneath on each side a black vein: bleed one or the other, but do not go too deep, as below are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the neck that are commonly bled are bled in two ways: either by piercing with a very wide flame-like martin or with an olive-shaped sharp instrument, and they are called 'anesil'; these are wide and slender according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of Martin's flame is very renowned, and it is so widespread as you can see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the swollen veins filled with visible thick blood, and containing thick and troubled blood; and this is the form of the olive flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	it is more pointed and sharp, and it is used to bleed delicate veins, where there is thin, yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The bleeding of the basilica, which is one of these veins, aids in treating illnesses affecting the throat, neck, chest, and abdomen; and the bleeder must be careful to avoid the artery located beneath it.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he cuts the artery, and blood flows out, it must be stanched as I have said; and the flame must not be gripped tightly, but held like a scalpel.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilic vein does not open clearly, you must extract it and replace it with another; or take a part of it, or heal in its place the vein within the arm: it opens clearly; and cauterize the wound as we have said before.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you wish to know the location of the wound, you must first extend the arm and touch the area until you feel the pulse; then mark the spot with a sign, bind the arm, and cauterize the wound as we said before; take care not to cut into the artery when you see the spot is swollen, for it is the artery: avoid it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see blood rising like the urine of a child, and it is red and thin, know that it is blood from an artery: act quickly then, press your finger on it for some time, then remove your finger if the bleeding stops, which often happens; bind the arm, and leave it be, do not move the patient; and let there be fear, and do not move them until they are healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not staunched, and it overcomes you, and no medic is present, then cut the artery if it is exposed, for this stops the head of the retreat; and staunch the blood.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a bark of fustic, slit it open, and take one half, binding it on well until the next day; if the blood is staunched, that is good; if not, then treat it as we have said with powders to staunch blood; and the staunching is not grievous in many cases due to the small size of the wound, and the strength of the arm's bond.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The bleeding of the vein in the middle helps as it draws blood from the head above and the body below, because it is composed of the basilica and cephalic veins, as we have said; and the bleeder must take care for the nerve that lies beneath, and if they cut too deeply into it, and find the nerve, it swells and the wound becomes grievous, and perhaps cannot heal; and this nerve often appears, and if it does not appear in some men due to its subtlety, then you must treat it with a sharp instrument; and avoid the nerve as best you can.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	Et if there is a vein between the two nerves, cut it lengthwise.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The bleeding of the cephalic vein is beneficial as it drains blood from the head and aids the eyes; one must bleed with caution near the olive-shaped flame or the martin's flame because this is the safest of all veins, for beneath it there are no nerves or arteries.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, one must seek the lightest place and not be too harsh if they miss the first time, for then one can start again; sometimes the vein swells in some people when pierced the first time but this is no great harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of bleeding depends on your assessment.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about bloodletting is that it was not introduced for the purpose of curing diseases but rather to maintain health and prevent future illnesses; and bloodletting should be done on one of the three veins which are: namely, the cephalic vein, the basilic vein, and the median cubital vein; and you must perform bloodletting at the beginning of Lent while fasting, and in autumn or winter after eating when signs of fullness appear; and it is best to do bloodletting on the first day or third day, two hours or three hours into the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	Bloodletting when administered for diseases has no determined time, but can be done whenever needed, day or night and at all times; and children should not be bled until they are fourteen years old, nor women who are pregnant before the fourth month up to the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	They ought not to bleed the old who have passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone wishes to be bled, no matter the reason, it is necessary that they first cleanse their intestines with a light clyster, if they have too much retained feces, so that the veins do not draw from the intestines any harmful superfluities which would damage the main organs; one should also not bleed those who are overly full of food, drunk, saturated with liquid, or suffering from dropsy; and nor should you attempt to bleed someone after an attack of colic, vomiting, diarrhea, excessive intercourse, or fatigue due to work, lack of sleep, fasting, or exertion in sports; and do not attempt this if the subject is lacking vitality because of some bodily injury or harm caused by a weapon; then purify their humors, drawing off any thick blood through diet and drink and medicines, provided you know how to use them properly; after which they should enter a bath - if there is no reason to prevent it - in order to thin out the blood, and bleed from the vein on the inner side of the elbow, as we have said before; the subject must then be guarded against any further labor or exertion that day, likewise lust or similar activities; the patient should remain calm and happy, whilst the one who is bleeding them stands above them, rubbing their arm two or three times until they feel a throbbing in the veins, at which point he tightens his grip with moderate force on the arm - too tight and the blood cannot flow properly. Then he moistens the iron with an old oil, then puts his left hand below where he intends to bleed them so that the vein doesn't collapse or break when it's cut;
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that escape like cords into the wound, and some of them are filled with windiness, so that when you place a flame on it, it retreats from the flame, and cannot open the vein; and thus is one among these things; if one opens the wound, then the wound becomes too narrow - for this reason, one must be careful in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the wound opens for the first time, it is good; but if not, one should try again a little below or above that place, unless the area has swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the area has swollen and the patient is afraid, one should wait for a day or two without binding the arm: perhaps some hot abscesses will appear; do not enter the bath, but instead try again to open the wound if you wish; if the hole is small, let the blood flow out carefully - you may doubt that it won't drain enough blood as you want, so apply fire directly onto this same opening; operate a little above the swollen area unless the wound is tiny. This happens often when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the place is swollen, do not restart the wound, and apply a poultice of oil, as it reduces the body's blood flow, and in this place, oil has a cooling effect. Thus administer an oil-based ointment for each dressing that treats open wounds to stop bleeding; this same method produces good results when using triacle (a medicinal syrup) or egg whites, when applied topically; they are so subtlely draw out the blood and separate it when it is too great.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a large abscess forms there which occurs many times, especially when it has not been properly dressed and the wound opening is small, then you must act quickly, and apply to the place warm sponge soaked in water and salt, and hold it for an hour; you should do this after the bleeding from the wound stops. If after a few days some blackening or greening remains there, it will not be harmful; but if you see any of these signs, then use some aloe or myrrh mixed into gallic juice, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often abscesses and appearances occur in the healing of the basilica: so place your hand on it, and if you find the area soft when pressed with the hand, then this appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, avoid putting anything on it that we have mentioned, for perhaps the cut is close to an artery; but apply a dry poultice to harden the area, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw from each person's blood according to the quantity of its quality, and the colour of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if you see it as thick, let it flow until it becomes thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And for one who is full and strong, requiring blood extraction, make a wider wound, and let the flame be wide; for someone who is weak, do the opposite, and they must be bled little by little, often, and should be bled by making an oblique incision rather than pricking; this manner of bleeding is safe from excessive loss of blood and cutting nerves, and it is better than long or wide incisions.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for someone whose body requires bleeding, give them bread moistened in pomegranate juice; if they are heated, take blood three or four times; and if they have a cold constitution, feed them before the bleeding moistened bread with musky syrup or aromatic honey syrup with spices like pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and an odorous syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he loses consciousness due to excessive blood loss during the operation, it is necessary for him to drink meat broth and subtle fragrant syrup, and to use other things that we have mentioned in the section on fainting, for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to bleed his arm and perform another operation, it is necessary, when he is weakened by severe bleeding, that he bleed little by little, according to the amount of strength he has, continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if one wishes to bleed his arm after the first bleeding operation, and he has a strong constitution, then he should be bled seven hours after the first bleeding or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if one wishes to bleed in another part of the body, then he should be bled on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is much blood within the body that has already heated up, and causes fever; it must be drawn out in great quantity, and the opening widened until it ceases in remission; then you should reapply all the conditions of healing, and place your hand on their pulse as they heal, so death does not come to the place of remission, and this happens many times when the healer is negligent; and do not apply pressure strongly when you wish to free the arm, and make blood flow a second time, if the opening has closed; or if it curves, stretch out the arm quickly, for that would be bad; but leave it as it heals a second time; or prick at the tip of the flame, until the blood that is congealed exits through the vein's opening, and apply a small piece of linen soaked in water, pressing lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the wound is swollen, leave it alone and do not constrict it until the abscess has subsided.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood a second time, do so in the same place or in another vein, or even on the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein between the arms is bled instead of the one on the head because it is more accessible.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	The method of bleeding is as follows: the patient immerses their hand in warm water until the veins turn red; they are then tied loosely so that the vein stands out clearly, and now it is bled through its full length but not across or along it; make the incision wide open, and bleed close to where the fingers join the hand, and if blood does not come out, immerse the hand in warm water again, letting the blood flow into the water until enough has been drawn off; and do not re-immerse the hand in warm water if the patient is feverish because this is done more often in winter than in summer. And bleeding from this vein is safer than all other veins because there are no arteries or nerves here.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The bleeding of the right palm is beneficial for all diseases of the liver, and here's how: Stretch out the hand and immerse it in hot water until the vein swells up so that it shows; if the vein runs sideways and you cut straight across it, there will be no harm; but don't cut too deep because below all are nerves stripped bare of flesh; then put the hand back into hot water if blood has clotted in the wound and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn as much blood as is needed, apply oil and linen to the vein to seal the wound, and do likewise for each tube.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	Bleeding from the left hand is good for disease of the spleen, and do everything just as I told you about the right one.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The bleeding of the saphenous vein is beneficial for all diseases that affect areas below the waist, such as illnesses affecting the uterus, retention of urine, kidney disease, and similar ailments in the hips, legs, and lower extremities.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of its bloodletting is that the patient should immerse their foot in hot water, and rub over the vein until it ruptures, then bind it above the ankle joint; this vein lies at the ankle, and extends upwards along the leg towards the kidneys; bleed the larger kidney, or at the ankle, whichever moves more freely.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you bleed it over the foot, be careful not to damage the nerves underneath, and bleed across them as though cutting; let the blood flow freely.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot exit, place the foot in water, and let it thoroughly drain the vein.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the veins fail to open the first time, try again a second time slightly higher, as the skin is salty; do not worry about nerves, as we have said, and do likewise with the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The skin of the sciatic vein is found above the ankle bone, and its opening serves to alleviate hip pain when hot blood is present.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	The quality of its opening is such that the patient should enter the bath and hold above the ankle for four days while twisting, as otherwise the vein will not open; if it does open, cleanse it in every way you can, and clean through it; it is better to cut it open, because the skin is salty, and this area is very sensitive in many men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you cannot find it, then treat any line of the leg that appears between the heel and little toe, avoiding the nerves; let blood flow from where you wish to see it, and then release the ligature, cover with cotton, and bind it tight; now she is healed.
des sainies de ventouse	cupping incisions
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cupping glasses are made of horn, or bronze, or glass; and cupping is done in two ways: either by drawing out blood, or without puncturing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this non-puncturing cupping is also done in two ways: either using only fire, or without fire; and the cupping that involves puncturing and blood extraction is performed at fourteen places on the body, some of which are all over the head; others are on the neck; two more are under each armpit; one below the chin; another one on each shoulder; then there are cups for the loins, for both arms, for both legs, and finally for both ankles; but this cupping does not draw out blood but only minor veins scattered in the flesh, and so it doesn't weaken a person like bleeding from a vein would do; neither type of cupping should be administered either with or without fire to any sickness that comes from excess until all such fullness is removed.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if it is necessary due to illness or for treatment purposes, cupping must be administered each hour at the beginning of the month, or towards the end, and in between; because there are those who, when they need cupping, suffer from a heavy head; and some experience fullness and redness on their face, neck, and forehead; while others find a drop of blood in their mouth, have an enlarged tongue, and spit up blood; and still, there are some who see blood, cuts, corpses, and similar things in their dreams.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, especially when it is midway through the month, we instruct them to undergo cupping after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The bleeding of the temple helps with the headaches... that affect the eyes, and it should not be done after draining all the body's fluids; this cupping takes place instead of bleeding from the head veins, and those who have a cold constitution must not use it or they who suffer from catarrh, for it does them great harm; and therefore the elderly must not do so nor those suffering from cold illnesses in the head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who heal often become forgetful, so it is necessary to place the cupping glass a little further down due to the fear of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	Cupping on the neck is in place of healing the head and brain, and for this reason, it helps with the narrowing of the chest, splitting of the canal of the lung, coughs, and fullness; one must be careful as if it holds too tightly, it can cause forgetfulness or stomach and heart issues.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	Cupping at the two collarbones is useful for headaches, eye pain, and migraines, as well as suffocation and tooth root pain; it replaces healing of the brain, and you must instruct the healer to extend their hand when placing it so they do not compress the artery or cause bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The swelling below the chin is due to mouth ailments and gum infections, as well as similar oral diseases, it occurs at the site of incisions on both lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Swelling in the shoulders is indicative of an illness caused by heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	Swelling in the armpit is just like that of the three veins in the arm, for it draws blood from these large vessels; instruct the surgeon not to make too deep an incision, as the area lacks flesh and has nerves and arteries underneath.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The swelling on the buttocks is indicative of haemorrhoids and underlying illnesses; it requires a large cup made of brass with strong suction power; if it were thin, it would break and cause major injuries.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The cups on the legs heal clearly, for they draw blood from all over the body, and are good for old pains of the kidneys, and of the uterus, and of the bladder, and bring down fevers; and they are placed on the two hips, and the two ankles, but nonetheless they weaken the body after long use, and cause fainting in many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply the cup is that you put it in place first while empty, and suck it firmly, and press it down quickly, and move it evenly, and do not stop until you see the area red and swollen, and the redness of the blood appears; then withdraw, and reposition the cups, and be mindful of the condition of the body, for some have tough flesh, and others tender skin: so one must strike only once, and make wide wounds, and somewhat deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to strike twice: the first time to thin out the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to strike a third time; and when we want to draw out small amounts of blood, we only need to strike once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want to draw out a large amount of blood, we strike often; and if the blood is thick, it must be struck perfectly, and the result is that the heart is pierced suddenly, and it is necessary for those with thick and hard skin, and who have narrow veins, to anoint the cupping glass orifices with aperient and dissolutive oil: if it is in summer, violet oil, almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil; and if it is in winter, cress oil, lily oil, chamomile oil, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is large and cold, take almond oil, or oil of balm, or dill oil, and their likes.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one who is healing has tender flesh and large pores, it should not be oiled, but instead it should be washed after the fomentation with rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or squash water, or china root water, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And for those with excessive moisture, rise easily with myrtle water, or sumac water, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those with large excesses should be treated with old wine, or water from a fig, or a decoction of dill or chamomile, and others like these; they ought not to be cupped before the bath nor in it, but after the bath for an hour or two; neither ought they sleep after the fomentation, but instead lie down when one must do a fomentation and when one is doing it.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And take care if the patient is choleric and their blood is too thin and inflamed; they should eat cold things like pomegranates and endive and lettuce at ease, similar things, drink little wine, eat pork fat, and moist meat.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And for those with a cold constitution, take honey syrup and medium aromatic wine, which is between old and new, eat little, drink little wine, eat pork fat, small birds, and pigeons; on the day they are cupped, they should drink more than eat; sometimes give some men treacle or nutmeg before or after cupping to strengthen principal members; although this thins blood, those who already have hot blood must not take it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The cups which are applied without any wounding are those that are placed on the liver, and on the spleen, podagra, on the belly, and buttocks, kidneys, and hip; for these parts do not tolerate being wounded, and it is done only to attract blood from one member to another as we also apply them on breasts when a baby suckles milk; in order to remove the viscidity that is present in such part as we place cups on belly or buttocks so as to diminish its dimensions; and for removing pain caused by concretions, calculi, if perchance it attracts concretion through its attractive power, or causes calculus to descend from its site. In this way it acts when applied on the liver and spleen where there is retention of flatulence and these cups are administered empty so as to suck only; sometimes they are administered together with fire, at other times filled with warm water like in diseases of pleurisy; and such a cup is filled with hot water alone or some herb suitable for this.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The way to apply a fire cupping device is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And let it be two fingers wide and half a palm deep, with a small hole on its side in the middle, just enough to push a needle through, and made of brass, soft in front so as not to hurt the patient when applied to the limb; and have in the middle an iron or steel bar, to hold a burning candle, and these come in various sizes according to the disease and age of those who use them; for cupping devices used on children are different from those used on the elderly, and thin people require different ones than fat people.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one must thus place this cupping device on the limb: take a wax candle or taper and put it inside the cupping device through the bar in its center, so that the flame is at the bottom of the cup to prevent burning the patient; then place it on the limb with your fingers over the hole we mentioned before, so when you want to release the vapors, lift off the cup and take the taper as before, and repeat this process often if needed.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the cupping treatment that is applied for pleurisy, it is completely airtight, with no tube or opening, and is only administered when it is full of water, being placed solely on the affected limb. And this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Cupping is only applied to those body parts where cupping cannot be directly administered due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar areas; also to the bare bone, like fingers or toes, and other similar parts. The quality of this treatment requires that when you find leeches that are in clear, clean water without any impurities, take them out; place them overnight in clean water so they become familiarized and have nothing in their bellies; then bleed the limb with a lancet and cupping, rubbing it until it is red, and apply the leeches. When they are full and fall off, if this is an area where cupping can be applied, do so, for it will prove very beneficial afterward.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If this does not work, then apply a hot compress first, and afterward with cold water, it is very effective, and then apply a poultice; if the wound heals too quickly after the application of leeches, wet a piece of linen cloth in cold water and place it on top until the bleeding has stopped; if the bleeding becomes excessive, apply crushed vitriol or gallnuts and similar substances until it stops; you can also put half of a peeled broad bean pod over the wound and leave it there until it dries up at the wound site, this will staunch the flow now; if more is required, take other leeches.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the leeches do not want to take hold, rub the wound with fresh blood, or prick it with a needle until blood appears, and then place them on top; as soon as they sense the presence of blood, they will attach themselves; once you see that they are feeding, sprinkle some powder of aloe and crushed psyllium or ash over them, and they will now stay put.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it deals with setting fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, my dear son, that if foolish physicians neglect this chapter and never turn to the ancient books or read any letters in them; for this reason science is neglected in our land, since I have never found a good one among them, nor do they know anything except through the science of these ancient books, where I have studied so much that I have treated their science and by experiment and through the experience of my life; and I have described to you in this chapter what it contains, having abridged it at the end and shown clearly the forms of instruments employed, as I did in these two previous chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is necessary, therefore, that we say in the prologue of this book the main points of the words and chapters where the sage puts his understanding, and remains focused on truth, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	When a fracture or dislocation or twisting or breaking occurs to someone, you must quickly bleed the patient on both sides if nothing else hinders you, such as bodily weakness, children, or elderly; unless the weather is too hot or too cold; and avoid eating cold foods like salads, pigeon meat, and goat meat, and do not drink wine, eat fatty meats, nor overeat flesh foods that fill the veins with blood until you are certain there is no hot abscess or discharge of matter to the limb. Then may the patient return to his former condition which he was used to govern himself in.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	When the broken bone begins to heal, one must feed the patient with nourishing meats that promote growth and have viscosity, such as wheat cooked in water, rice, eggs, feet, cow stomach, chicken eggs, fresh fish, strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For too much nourishment causes swelling and delays healing of the fracture.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the broken bones of the elderly and decrepit cannot heal or fuse well according to their natural state due to the dryness of their limbs; nor can those who are too young as their bones are still soft like those of small children. But there is a cure: place large splints above the broken bone which bind and join the limb together, strengthening it as it was before; do not cease this treatment entirely but continue until healed and for this one must nourish with nourishing meats as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from that of the arm, or the leg, and I shall tell you in this chapter all the types of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is fracture that requires resetting, and another by sharpening, just like the cut of a quill to write with.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is fracture accompanied by wound, or just a small crack in the bone.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And for each type of fracture there is its own method and proper instrument for restoration according to the memory that returns when in place; and bone fracture is known by twisted position, clearly visible externally, and sounding hollow under pressure from the hand; and where there is no deformity nor sound upon touch, and patient feels little pain, then there is probably no fracture but rather a twist or small crack or hairline fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	You must not move it by hand, but apply the following medicines, then hold it firmly yet gently.
