Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is close to the root of the thigh, then one bandage should be towards the wrist, and the other bandages below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	Also, if the break is close to the knee, then the bandages should be placed near the knee, and the stretching should be done below; have the assistants hold the bone equal with their two hands, so it aligns with its natural shape, and then apply the plaster cast, binding it well, unless an abscess appears.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is hot abscess, let it cool down before returning to your work and treatment; the binding should be done in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	You must wrap the fracture with a hard bandage doubled in II or III layers, leaving the excess, then turn the leg so that the heel reaches the groin's root, and pass the long thread between the thigh and the leg, below the knee, and bring the thread's end above; then turn back over the leg and the thigh with the bandage, then place stars on the fracture, and put a star on the bone of the leg; then fill the empty space between the leg and the thigh with soft cloths to equalize the pressure, then start tying firmly III or IV twists over the fracture; and as you go up from the fracture, lessen the pressure; then tighten the II ends of the thread that you passed between the leg and the thigh, and tie III stars that are above, then return below to the thread's end until you reach near the foot; and bind it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it like this, waiting for no abscess or swelling or other similar thing.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, undo it and address what has occurred, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that are stuck, you must remove them if possible; and if one cannot, then one must split the place and draw forth with force; and treat [the wound] as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the thigh is broken and fixed with pins, as in the hip or arm; nevertheless, during such a restoration, the patient does not suffer.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And understand that the thigh is restored in L days, or perhaps a little less or more, according to the variations of constitutions [i.e., different patients].
de la ruelle dou genoil	Of the groove of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the alley of the knee there is little breakage, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is only a crack or a hole, and this occurs with all wounds, whether felt as pain or not, and one feels well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	One should restore it by placing something equal to what is round at its two sides so that they are joined as close as possible; then apply the plaster and place a round rod if needed, holding it tight as required, then follow all the arrangements we have mentioned for other breaks, such as hot abscesses and similar; provide each accident with what suits it until it heals.
de la brisure de la jambe	On the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is rightfully called "mustelz," and the other is named "foscile"; they both suffer breaks similar to those occurring in the arm, and for this reason their restoration is like that of the arm, equally so, and the treatments are all found therein. If these two bones break together, the leg becomes twisted on all sides.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the subtle bone is broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the thick bone is broken, one feels great pain and it shows clearly; it turns downwards.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Therefore, provide extension and make it even, and bind the bones equally; however, if the break is ugly and there are multiple fragments, let the extension be less extensive and lighter; ease accordingly to your strength.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, and le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of broken bones in the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no break, but in the bones of the foot a break can occur and at the toes sometimes only cracking takes place in various situations.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a break in the bones of the foot, and you see these bones protruding from one another, then have the patient put their foot on the ground, as if they want to walk, and then place your foot on theirs, where the bones are raised, then press until they return to their places; then apply a plaster cast and bandages above, and place underneath the sole of the foot a small board with two fingers' width, then bind it to the foot properly, then wrap it with cloth and other things you need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, untie the bandage, for you will find the bones equalized, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	If there are any of the toes broken, restore them as we have said for fingers; then place in the broken toe a peg according to its length and somewhat wider, then put beneath the foot that board I mentioned, and strain it suitably; if there be two or three, or more, broken, place on each toe a peg according to its size wrapped in a piece of linen, and fasten the board beneath the foot; let it rest on the head of the board outside the front of the foot so that it holds well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things I have said about other fractures that we have mentioned previously; attend to each fracture as it should be done.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	Of the broken bone of the wrist
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman's nature is broken, make her sit with her legs spread wide, then lean her towards her back and hold her from behind; then fill the gap in the nature of the patient with cotton, putting as much in there as fits; stand up the woman and lift her back little by little, until the cotton pops out at the entrance of her nature, bringing the bone together with it; when she wants to pee, remove the cotton, and once she has peed put it back in again, do this for seven days or so: the fracture will be restored, and if you wish, take a goat's bladder, tie a reed to its hole, push all of the bladder into her nature, then blow hard through the reed until the bladder is inflated inside there; her nature will mend where it was broken, then fill with cotton again and leave for some days until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the wrist in man or woman is broken, restore it as we have said for the hip bone; and these breaks are not hidden from those who apply themselves and use what they learn from my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the break shows itself in many ways, showing the correct path to restoration; understand this then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In a broken penis, take the gullet of a goose and insert it inside; then wrap it with soft cloth around, and leave it for three days so it heals quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	For break with wound:
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	He who has a break with wound, especially if it is large like the bone of the thigh or shoulder, must be treated now as we have described for treatment of wounds.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, treat it with vitriol poultice, if you have nothing else, then repeat the treatment to restore the fracture that same hour or day, unless hot abscesses arise.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	If hot abscesses appear, leave the treatment until the ninth day, until the abscess has calmed down, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you would cause a bad outcome.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	If the broken bone is apparent on an exposed heart, you must set it gently with your hands in a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension does not match your hand to align it evenly, reset it with this iron tool which is seven or eight inches long, and its width depends on the size of the wound; and for this, the surgeon needs to grip it firmly with three or four fingers, according to his need in each treatment of a fracture; and let it be round and slightly thick so that it does not bend under compression on the limb during your work, and let it be pointed at the front, and thicker towards the middle like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche", therefore the curved head must be placed on top of the visible bone; push it once until it returns and becomes even with each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle and the instrument cannot properly grasp the bone, then you must cut off the head of the bone until the instrument has enough power to do so.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot reset the bone as we have said, then cut it with an appropriate instrument, whether a cutting or sewing tool of your choice; afterwards remove what remains in the bone of roughness and small flakes.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is reset, and the patient feels great pain afterward, know that it is not yet in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	Si make sure it is in its place, then moisten a cloth with black astringent wine, and properly so if it is in summer; do not put any ointment or other oily substance on the wound, for this will cause suppuration and corruption; administer stars when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, cut the cover all around according to the size of the wound, and be careful that the wound is not constrained by the fracture; many a time have foolish doctors done this, and they have brought death or corrosion upon the patient; let the constriction be softer and gentler than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you fear that evil accidents may come to pass, as we have said, and you find pain in the place, then do not put stars on it; but wrap around it, instead of using stars, hard cloths, and bind them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that the wound is inflamed, remove what you have applied to it entirely, and put on a healing ointment such as tetrafarmacon and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	You must loosen the limb twice a day, in the morning and at night, until it is fused and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be bandaged in such a way that the bowstring runs downward slightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if after many days it does not heal but becomes inflamed again, know that there are small pieces of bone present, which is why you must probe the wound with a needle and remove all these loose pieces that cause such pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula develops at the site or any other form of corruption occurs, you must treat it according to what he says in his chapter beforehand.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	When the bone is broken and exposed on the limb, like the thighbone or shoulder blade, and other similar large bones, do not extract it as death often ensues. Leave it until it rots; perhaps it will fall out by itself after twenty or thirty days; then treat the wound if you can, otherwise leave it be.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	Scabs that form over the healing.
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often see patients after they have recovered from their fracture, especially when it is near the joint and the deformity of the limb is evident, which sometimes prevents the limb from performing its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care if it is fresh: administer styptic medicines such as aloe, incense, myrrh, and saracolle, acacia gum, and similar substances; prepare any of these or all together with styptic wine, egg white, or wax; place on the night in a tight bandage, don't loosen for two days; then release it and start another one until the nodules are gone; you can also strap them to a well-made wooden board as wood has the property to reduce swelling of limbs; if they have already turned hard like stone and must be removed, cut out what is apparent and scrape off the remainder so that all traces are gone.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	Of the member which is weak after treatment
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the bone fracture is healed, and afterward the limb remains weak and delicate, it occurs for many reasons: one being that it was bound too tightly, and not as it should have been; or because there were too many bandages, preventing nourishment from reaching the limb; or due to excessive draining; or because of overly large movements, not at the right time; or because there is little blood in their body, thus making them weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the treatment is that you make the patient eat, and soften their body so that blood multiplies within them; administer a bath to them, and provide joy and leisure; then place pitch on the limb so that the pitch attracts great nourishment, and often moisten it with warm water until nourishment reaches the limb; and return it to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	A joint twisted after the injury.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the broken bone is visible, and the shape of the limb is ugly, nonetheless it does not lose its natural function: do not believe the fools who say that one should break the limb anew, and many a fool has done this in our land; and these practices are condemned, resulting in great harm, even death; however, if the inflammation and pain are fresh, they should be treated with warm water, or softening herbs cooked, such as leaves of mallow, roots, and honeysuckle, and similar things; then apply a softening poultice, like well-made aquilano plaster, and take the mucus of mallow, mix it with chicken fat or sesame oil, and make a poultice out of it; alternatively, you can take fatty figs, grind them with fenugreek flour, and similar medicines that facilitate healing.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the swelling is removed by continually and thoroughly rubbing with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	Make gentle movements to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	If the tendon is shrivelled and hardened like stone, and must be removed with an iron instrument, cut it away as close to the bone as possible using a fine, sharp incision; then apply stitches and take care in treating the wound.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs to anyone, you must now reset it without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	If you delay, the joint swells, and by chance if it is reset painfully to its place; for this reason, one must not move it while swollen: often causing spasm and other pains; nevertheless, when this happens, make the patient bleed, then leave them alone until the abscess has healed; then bathe the limb in warm water and oil, then gently reset it, and treat each member as the cure progresses.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations of the head down to foot.
des mandibules	Of the jaws.
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, 
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns through various positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is complete and whole, you must reduce the dislocation quickly, without delay; in such a way that the assistant holds the patient's head, and with one of their hands they push on the mirror under the chin at the root of the dislocated jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is in two parts; and keep the other hand outside, to provide balance; instruct the patient to relax, their jaws, and move them around freely.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	The mirror is placed evenly until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if reducing it is difficult, especially if they are both jaws together, soak them in hot water and oil until they can be gently pulled back; do not delay the reduction as we have said before.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are repositioned evenly, and the patient's wound is closed without softening it, place on it moistened compresses in a cerote made of rose oil and wax, then lightly bind it with soft bandages; let the patient sleep on their back, with two cushions supporting their shoulders so that they cannot move them to either side, nor strain themselves by trying to chew, but take light food until the pains are gone, and keep their jaws bound; and thereafter eat what they wish in a gentle manner, not forcing open their mouth for eating or drinking, until the jaw is well healed and healthy.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be reset at once and fail to return to their original position, then fevers and sweating may follow, possibly accompanied by a loosening of the bowels or even vomiting up clear fluid.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, know that it is destruction; and many times the one it befalls dies within nine days.
de la forcelle	Of the fork.
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The fork cannot be reset from the sides within its limits; sometimes it is dislocated externally and this can be easily felt.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is as follows: let the patient lie often on their back and extend their arms; then press the place strongly with your palm and it will return to its position; afterwards apply a plaster and bandage, holding it in place; but the head that faces towards the neck cannot be reset; unless if possible, or if it is dislocated at some time, then reset it as we have described above; after this, put on the plaster and bind it with a bandage again, restraining it, and instruct the patient to rest until they are healed. The same procedure applies for the shoulder head when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Know that the shoulder is dislocated in three ways: thus one is that it dislocates at the part of the socket below; and the second is at the part of the chest; and perhaps it dislocates above, and this happens rarely; and it does not dislocate behind for the shoulder, nor inside toward the nerves; and many times it dislocates below towards the socket, especially in those who have little flesh, for it falls out easily; in those who have enough flesh, it falls with difficulty, and enters with difficulty.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And perhaps it happens to some men by blow or fall, and the shoulder swells from a hot abscess, and one thinks that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	You must therefore test it until you are certain; then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	The dislocation is recognized when the arm falls towards the shoulder blade and there is an obvious difference between the affected shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find a noticeable disparity between them; and at the head of the shoulder, there is a depression, and beneath the shoulder blade, on touching the head of the shoulder, it feels like an egg; and the patient cannot bring their hand to their nose or make any movements; and if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you will find it clearly upon touch; and this type of dislocation is not difficult to reset when it is recent or in children.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	The method is for the assistant to lift the patient's hand upwards and then place their fists beneath the shoulder blade while lifting the joint forcefully upward into its correct position; the assistant should raise the patient's hand and stretch it upwards before placing it underneath, and this will bring relief.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said in ordinary days afterward, then the patient must be bathed in warm water; and bring him a moistening and softening remedy, such as a decoction of alum, fenugreek, and sweet clover in water, and let it be administered; then remember to place the patient on his back, and put beneath him an even woolen cushion that is neither too soft nor too hard, then have the physician place their heel on the cushion, lift the head of the shoulder virtuously, and pull the patient's hand; and another assistant should hold the patient's head so it does not move downward; that shoulder will return immediately, and if you wish to reset it according to this manner: and make sure there is a third man present who is stronger than the patient; he must be upright facing the side of the patient, then push his shoulder beneath the patient's cushion, lifting the cushion upwards so that the patient hangs in the air; while another assistant pulls the patient's hand downward toward their belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, weigh them down with something heavy, and the dislocation will return now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And it is also reset in another manner: take a long pole and drive it into the ground, so that the shoulder aligns like a piston, neither too thick nor too thin; then place it beneath the patient, with soft cloths underneath, and have the patient lie down along the length of the pole; extend their arm on the other side very gently, and the joint will return to its place gradually; if it does not wish to return despite all these methods we have mentioned, perform this cure: take a pole two arms in length and four palms wide, with a rounded head so as to perfectly enter through underneath the shoulder blade, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then lie above the head of the wounded man a cloth that does not hurt him and put it under the arm of the patient; spread his arms on top of the long board, tie up the shoulder to the board then fasten the arm at the head end by the hand, place the other arm along a peg in an upright partition with hands hanging down and leave the body let hang from the opposite side: the joint is replaced now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, no matter how it was done, you must put under the arm a wad of equal wool then apply the plaster prepared with flour powder, incense and egg white over all shoulder and around, then tighten the strap under the arm accordingly, return the binding on top of the plaster, embrace the hand to his neck, and leave hands in that position.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And he should eat little, until the limb is strengthened, for then it will heal faster; and after five or seven days, let him eat more, and move [the limb]; if it is firm and not softened, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint has moved out of place due to moisture or for any other reason, you must apply cauterization to three openings, as described before in the chapter on cauterization.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this and it dislocates again after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and he cannot lift his arm upwards, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is either cut, stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be put back in place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is towards the arm, and the breasts, or at the back, is caused by an impact, and a stretch of hands, and it should be treated elsewhere; heal until it is cured.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing process, there is cracking in the limb, and delayed movement, let the patient bathe frequently until this cracking eases, and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	Of shoulder dislocation:
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the shoulder joint is repeatedly dislocated and returns to its place; if it is fully dislocated, especially from front to back, and the dislocation is not corrected because it can be clearly seen and felt; and it varies depending on each person's anatomy.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick person's wound with the healthy one, you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	Because the joint is dislocated, and cannot bend the arm or reach their shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And you must reset it before any abscesses form, for if an abscess forms, it will be difficult to reset; and perhaps it cannot be completely reset, especially when it is at the back; thus it is worse than other dislocations, causing even more pain, and sometimes death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration occurs when it is such that one can reset it; you extend their arm with both your hands; their arms should be spread out, and their palms facing towards you all around, above and below; push the joint into its socket or at the root of their palm until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is at the front, it returns when he bends his hand towards his hand, and press against the root of the palm the bone which has come out of joint.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	If it does not want to return to its place, then administer strong extension; while one minister extends the arm, let the other extend it too so that it doesn't move during the extension; then turn the arm from side to side; after you have wrapped a long and wide double piece of cloth around it; when the doctors has united the joint with the hand, anoint it with some oil to soften the joint, then press on the joint firmly until it returns; once it is in place, apply dry poultice with egg white on top, strain it tightly, bend the arm over the patient's neck and leave for a few days, then untie it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, untie the bandage and leave it alone; but if you see that the joint does not tighten properly, then reapply the plaster and the bandage, leaving it there for a few days until it sets firmly, before you undo it again.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels soreness after the realignment of the joint, and it becomes inflamed, bathe and gently rub it, pressing until it is soothed; or you can apply to the joint a poultice made with fat mutton wool, leaving this on for a day and night, then remove it and place the limb in a bath; when he sweats, gently rub the joint, then reapply the poultice before entering the bath once more; do this twice or three times until it is healed; if you see any remaining inflammation, apply warm fresh dung mixed with butter to the area, and it will return to its proper condition.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand is dislocated and its return is light compared to other joints. Nevertheless, it must be reset immediately when it is dislocated, unless the place is swollen or an abscess forms there.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the resetting is such that you place the sick hand on a table, and the assistants stretch out the hand, and align it so that they put their palm above the joint, and push until it returns to its proper position. Nevertheless, one must ensure that it is in place; thus, make the patient lay the back of his hand on a table during extension and resetting.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, make the patient lay the back of their hand on the table and have the assistants place their hand above that joint's position.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it comes back now, that's good But if not, restrain with healing compresses hot abscesses, and leave them like this without restarting.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot endure it, and you cannot put it back in place after some days, the joint remains dislocated; and it causes no harm to the patient as long as the hand is weakened, and unable to grasp anything at all: then know that the nerves are cut, or the artery; there is no other instrument but cauterization near the site, and perhaps nothing else will help.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, apply the poultice we mentioned, then restrain it and leave it for five days, then release it and leave it like that.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it properly, and there is any tearing, then bathe it with warm water, and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	Of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Sometimes the finger of the hand is dislocated on each side, sometimes on the back of the palm or on the belly; then extend the finger, and push the dislocation with your fingers until it returns, then hold the head of the finger, and bend it towards the part where it is dislocated; leave it for two days, and then make it equal that day; at night, bind it as we have said, and untie it during the day, making it move, and rebind it at night; do this often until it is narrow, and do likewise if it is dislocated on the palm of the hand, doing as you have done before until it is healed; and do the same when it is dislocated elsewhere.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Of dislocation of the spine from the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine from the back or neck is dislocated, or there are multiple dislocations, there is no cure, for death hurries the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that gas escapes involuntarily, and they cannot control it, and often parts of the body become weak, such as both thighs or arms or one side; and often the spine is affected in four places; this which affects the rear is called "gilbositez": the cure is to reverse if gilbositez came from childhood: there is no cure nor full recovery.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from a fall or blows or similar things, the ancient methods of treatment with lengthy speeches have little benefit overall; but I have shortened them according to my intent, and crafted instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the hump which develops on the front of the chest, no surgeon or medical expert has any knowledge; and also regarding the one that comes directly at II sides, it cannot be cured unless that which properly comes to the back, as I said; And it is such that the patient should lie extended on his face in a level place, and have some strain beneath him so he does not hurt himself; then insert an iron bar into the head strongly embedded into the ground, and another at the feet, and tie a cord over the shoulder blades of the patient, and another to the hips, knees, and ankles; And two helpers should pull on the cords, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two bars; and they must be firmly fixed, both the iron bar as we have said, and the doctor puts his palms onto the spine forcefully until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return to its place with this treatment, take a board that is three arms long and place it below the wall, let the patient be on their side, push the head of the board beneath the wall, then put the middle of the board over the spine; have the surgeon put his feet over the other end of the board and press hard until it returns to its place; if you wish, do this with a device that twists in the direction of the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	Put two pegs in the head of the patient's arm and another towards their feet, leaving a palm-length space between each; have a hole in each peg where the rod runs through, and make sure these are firmly placed in the ground so they do not move; between every two pegs put one turning peg on top that has two small pegs of one palm length to turn it; then tie the rope that is amongst the holes to the turning peg towards the head, and another rope from towards their feet to the other turning peg; each assistant turns their rod with all their might while the master ensures an even spine as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is equalized, apply a drying plaster with an abundance of egg, then pack with linen swabs, and then use the rod of a tablet three fingers long to probe the site of deformity and the healthy part of the spine, then bind it with a bandage as we have said, and let the patient use fine nourishment until they are healed; and if anything should happen at the end of healing, you must administer softening and soothing medicines along with the rod that we mentioned earlier; sometimes an iron probe is administered, and other times there appears in the last vertebra of the back a protrusion which people believe to be dislocation; but it is bone that has appeared, so one shouldn't presume: perhaps this could lead to death.
des dislocations de la hainche	Of hip dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	The joints of the hip and shoulder are susceptible only to dislocations, not like other joints; and the joint of the hip can be dislocated in four ways: inward and outward, and forward and backward; more commonly it is dislocated inwardly, rarely forward or backward.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the sign of an inward dislocation is that when you join the affected leg with the healthy one, it will be longer and the patient's knee will appear more prominent than the healthy one; they cannot bend their leg forward at the knee; and the area beside the hip is swollen with a hot abscess because the head of the thigh bone has come away.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him to whom it comes out of order is such that these accidents are contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of him to whom it happens in front are such that he stretches his leg according to its length; however, he does not bend his knee without pain, and if one wants him to walk, he cannot go forward, and he holds back his urine, and his ankle swells, and when he goes, he steps on his heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him to whom it happens behind are such that he cannot spread his knee, nor bend it, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the head of the thigh bone is in place beneath the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The reattachment of this type of dislocation is such that you must reset it if the dislocation is old and remains in its position, so there is no need for treatment; and it should not be assumed as a simple task.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And for the one with a fresh dislocation, which has four types of dislocation, you must hurry and reset the joint, stretching it both inside and out, and moving it right and left; perhaps it will return to its place, and no other treatment is needed.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	If it does not return with this method, you must prepare a strong assistant and stretch the leg firmly with both hands, or use a strap tied above the knee; another assistant holds the end of the strap; they all pull together upwards and downwards until the patient is lifted off the ground and left hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common to four similar cases, and if the dislocation returns, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, it is necessary to apply treatment in a similar way. When the dislocation is within the groin, you must place the patient on their healthy side and then put a bandage around the root of the thigh and below the hip joint, stretching it upwards towards the hip and the inguinal ligament; another assistant should then embrace the upper part of the affected thigh with his arms and stretch it outwards strongly: this will bring it back into place at once; this kind of dislocation is easier to treat than other kinds.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot secure it in the way we have described, then bind together the two feet of the patient with a strong soft bandage across both heels and knees; let the affected leg be extended two inches more than the other one; then hang him by his head from a pole so that he is two arms' length above ground level; order another assistant to embrace the top of the thigh, while yet another hangs alongside the patient embracing the thigh tightly: this will quickly restore the joint.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocations are on the outside, the patient lies down as we have said for someone with curvature of the spine, and he binds the joint over the sick leg properly, and also on the foot; then he places two heated iron rods, one at the head and another at the feet, then insert the rod between the thighs of the patient in the area of the dislocation; and let moistened towels be placed around it so that they do not burn the patient, then extend each minister towards him, and have the surgeon place the dislocated joint equally with his hand.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, that is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place him on the table, and press as we have said for curvature of the spine, and let the patient lie on his healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	Et when the dislocations are forward, you must extend the affected leg gradually, and as I said; have the assistant apply pressure above the afflicted ankle, then push with the other hand, and stretch it downwards toward the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is outward, you should not stretch the affected leg downward or lift it off the ground, instead, position it as if the hip were dislocated outward, as we mentioned regarding the arrangement on both hips; have them lie on their face and apply the strapping method described earlier, pressing on the joint with a flat surface; it is correct when the patient can extend their legs equally, align the thighs, then apply the plaster cast and wrap firmly so that the hip does not move; they must rest for three or four days, after which you remove the bandages, reapply the plaster cast; if you see that the limbs are aligned, repeat the process as before, leaving it on for another three days; then remove the bandage again, and have them gently walk around until their limb is strengthened.
de la dislocation dou genoil	Of knee dislocation
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knees are dislocated in three ways: that is to say, inwardly and outwardly, and behind; but they do not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the sign of this is that you command the patient to bend their leg at the thigh, and if it does not reach his thigh, know that he is dislocated; and the restoration of all these cases is for you to make the patient sit straight, and extend his leg as much as possible, and put your back on his face, and place his foot on your feet; then take his knee in your palms and pull it between your two hands, then bend both sides of the knee very hard; and another minister extends his foot so that the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that he bends his leg lightly at his thigh; then apply a plaster, and make him stretch his leg to his thigh, and bind them together tightly for three or four days; then untie it; and do not let the patient walk until the limb is strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not broken, administer strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	Of heel dislocation:
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are sometimes bruised, and sometimes fully dislocated, inside and out.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the sign of this is that the ankle is swollen, and more so on the part where it is dislocated; its reset should be done gently, and one must stretch it lightly by hand when it is only bruised.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is completely dislocated, you must have the patient sit upright, and hold them by the ministers (assistants) except for with the leg, above the ankle; then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then with your left hand twice, then stretch it upwards, and push the foot upwards strongly; do this twice, as we have said, both in pulling and pushing the foot; if it returns, that is good; if not, repeat the work, for it will return; and if it cannot be returned thus, then have the patient lie on their back on the ground, and firmly fix a pole into the earth between their thighs, securing the cloth around it so as to not hurt the patient; then have one minister hold the thigh, and another extend the foot by hand or with a cord tied above the ankle; then stretch each minister equally, and let the pole be adjacent to the patient's thighs to hold them while stretching; then place the mirrors (instruments) equally over the dislocation with your hands, and another minister holds the healthy leg underneath, and the dislocation will quickly return.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is at the point of being fixed, apply the plaster and pads on top, hold it firmly, bind the foot to the leg, and secure the tendons above the ankle from behind, ensuring the bindings are not too tight; leave it for two or three days, if the bindings loosen, tighten them again; then release the bindings after either the third or fourth day, forbidding the patient to walk for four days; and if he walks before this term is up, it is not secure that it won't dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if hot abscesses arise there, you must treat them as we have said elsewhere until they are healed.
des dois	twice.
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the thumb is dislocated, it should be gently stretched without exertion, which is an easy task.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any joint of the foot or back, you must make the patient sit on a flat surface or on a straight table, and place your foot on what appears to be these joints, then press hard with your foot until it returns; when it is aligned and nothing appears wrong, place a two-footed table under the sole of their foot, then strain them firmly, and leave for three days, then untie (the bandages); let them rest until they are healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	Of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound occurs along with dislocation and it needs to be restored, often the patient dies: do not be presumptuous in your treatment if you are not wise in this art and have not practiced it long enough, and if you are not compassionate and merciful nor bold; first use things that cool abscesses at the beginning, and leave the patient in God's hands if you see no hope of health; and when you do see some hope, then reset the limb before any hot abscess forms; once the limb is in place, administer treatments to cool the hot abscess, and treat the wound as it requires with drying ointments; and if along with dislocation there is a fracture and small bones are displaced, remove them, and do what we have said for simple illnesses; beware of doubt and fear as I mentioned, because this will affect you according to your Creator's will, and for the safety of your soul and body.
Amen	Amen
